Following the post-glacial flooding of the [[Persian Gulf|Persian Gulf basin]], debris from the [[Tigris–Euphrates river system|Tigris–Euphrates river]] formed a substantial delta, creating most of the land in present-day  and establishing the present coastlines. One of the earliest evidence of human presence in  dates back to the [[Mesolithic]] era (c. 8000 BC). Historically, most of present-day  was part of ancient [[Mesopotamia]].

During the [[Ubaid period]] (c. 5500–3700 BC),  was the central site of interaction between the peoples of [[Mesopotamia]] and Neolithic [[Eastern Arabia]], including [[Bahra 1]] and [[H3 ()|site H3]] in [[Subiya, |Subiya]]. The Neolithic inhabitants of  were among the world's earliest maritime traders. One of the world's earliest [[reed boats]] was discovered at [[H3 ()|site H3]] dating back to the Ubaid period. Other Neolithic sites in  are located in Khiran and [[Sulaibikhat]].

[[Mesopotamian]]s first settled in the  island of [[Failaka Island|Failaka]] in 2000 BC. Traders from the [[Sumer]]ian city of [[Ur]] inhabited Failaka and ran a mercantile business. The island had many Mesopotamian-style buildings typical of those found in [[]] dating from around 2000 BC. In 4000 BC until 2000 BC,  was home to the [[Dilmun civilization]]. Dilmun included Al-Shadadiya, [[Akkaz Island|Akkaz]], [[Umm an Namil Island|Umm an Namil]], and [[Failaka Island|Failaka]]. At its peak in 2000 BC, Dilmun controlled the [[Persian Gulf]] trading routes.

During the Dilmun era (from ca. 3000 BC), Failaka was known as "[[Agarum (toponym)|Agarum]]", the land of [[Enzak]], a great god in the Dilmun civilization according to Sumerian cuneiform texts found on the island. As part of Dilmun, Failaka became a hub for the civilization from the end of the 3rd to the middle of the 1st millennium BC. After the Dilmun civilization, Failaka was inhabited by the [[Kassites]] of [[Mesopotamia]], and was formally under the control of the [[Kassites#Kassite Dynasty of Babylon|Kassite dynasty of Babylon]]. Studies indicate traces of human settlement can be found on Failaka dating back to as early as the end of the 3rd millennium BC, and extending until the 20th century AD. Many of the artifacts found in Falaika are linked to Mesopotamian civilizations and seem to show that Failaka was gradually drawn toward the civilization based in [[Antioch]].
[[File:Achaemenid_Empire_500_BCE.jpg|right|thumb|The [[Achaemenid Empire]] at its greatest territorial extent]]
Under [[Nebuchadnezzar II]], the bay of  was under [[Babylonia]]n control. Cuneiform documents found in Failaka indicate the presence of Babylonians in the island's population. [[List of Kings of Babylon|Babylonian Kings]] were present in Failaka during the [[Neo-Babylonian Empire]] period, [[Nabonidus]] had a governor in Failaka and Nebuchadnezzar II had a palace and temple in Falaika. Failaka also contained temples dedicated to the worship of [[Shamash]], the Mesopotamian sun god in the Babylonian pantheon.

Following the [[Fall of Babylon]], the bay of  came under the control of the [[Achaemenid Empire]] (c. 550‒330 BC) as the bay was repopulated after seven centuries of abandonment. Failaka was under the control of the Achaemenid Empire as evidenced by the archaeological discovery of Achaemenid strata. There are [[Aramaic]] inscriptions that testify Achaemenid presence.

In fourth century BC, the [[ancient ]] colonized the bay of  under [[Alexander the Great]]. The ancient  named mainland  ''Larissa'' and Failaka was named ''[[Ikaros (Failaka Island)|Ikaros]]''. The bay of  was named ''Hieros Kolpos''. According to [[Strabo]] and [[Arrian]], Alexander the Great named Failaka ''Ikaros'' because it resembled the [[Aegean island|Aegean Island]] of that name in size and shape. Elements of [[ mythology]] were mixed with the local cults. "Ikaros" was also the name of a prominent city situated in Failaka. Large [[Hellenistic]] [[Towns of ancient #Military settlements|fort]]s and [[ temple]]s were uncovered. Archaeological remains of  colonization were also discovered in Akkaz, Umm an Namil, and Subiya.

[[File:Seleucid_Empire_alternative_map.jpg|left|thumb|The [[Seleucid Empire]] at its greatest extent]]
At the time of Alexander the Great, the mouth of the [[Euphrates|Euphrates River]] was located in northern . The Euphrates river flowed directly into the Persian Gulf via Khor [[Subiya, |Subiya]] which was a river channel at the time. Failaka was located 15 kilometers from the mouth of the Euphrates river. By the first century BC, the Khor Subiya river channel dried out completely.

In 127 BC,  was part of the [[Parthian Empire]] and the kingdom of [[Characene]] was established around [[Teredon]] in present-day . Characene was centered in the region encompassing southern Mesopotamia, Characene coins were discovered in Akkaz, Umm an Namil, and Failaka. A busy Parthian commercial station was situated in .

In 224 AD,  became part of the [[Sassanid Empire]]. At the time of the Sassanid Empire,  was known as ''Meshan'', which was an alternative name of the kingdom of Characene. Akkaz was a [[Parthian Empire|Partho]]-[[Sassanian]] site; the [[Zoroastrianism|Sassanid religion]]'s [[tower of silence]] was discovered in northern Akkaz. Late Sassanian settlements were discovered in Failaka. In [[Bubiyan Island|Bubiyan]], there is archaeological evidence of Sassanian to early Islamic periods of human presence as evidenced by the recent discovery of torpedo-jar pottery shards on several prominent beach ridges.

In 636 AD, the [[Battle of Chains]] between the Sassanid Empire and [[Rashidun Caliphate]] was fought in . As a result of Rashidun victory in 636 AD, the bay of  was home to the city of [[Kazma]] (also known as "Kadhima" or "Kāzimah") in the early Islamic era.

===1752–1945: Pre-oil===
{{see also|Sheikhdom of }}
[[File:MarinetimeMKuwaitAlshami.jpg|thumb|right|[[Al-Hashemi-II|Marine Museum]] in  City. Demonstrates the founding of  as a sea port for merchants.]]
In the early to mid 1700s, [[ City]] was a small [[fishing village]]. Administratively, it was a sheikhdom, ruled by [[sheikh]]s from the local [[Bani Khalid]] clan. Sometime in the mid 1700s, the [[Bani Utbah]] settled in  City. Sometime after the death of the Bani Khalid's leader Barak bin Abdul Mohsen and the fall of the [[Bani Khalid Emirate]], the Utub were able to wrest control of  as a result of successive [[Marriage of state|matrimonial alliances]].

In the latter half of the eighteenth century,  began establishing itself as a maritime [[port]] and gradually became a principal commercial center for the transit of goods between [[Baghdad]], , Persia, [[Muscat]], and the [[Arabian Peninsula]]. By the late-1700s,  had established itself as a trading route from the Persian Gulf to [[Aleppo]]. During the [[Ottoman–Persian War (1775–1776)|Persian siege of Basra in 1775–79]],  merchants took refuge in  and were partly instrumental in the expansion of 's boat-building and trading activities. As a result, 's maritime commerce boomed, as the  trade routes with Baghdad, Aleppo, [[Smyrna]] and [[Constantinople]] were diverted to  during this time. The [[East  Company]] was diverted to  in 1792. The East  Company secured the sea routes between ,  and the east coasts of Africa. After the Persians withdrew from [[Basra]] in 1779,  continued to attract trade away from Basra. The flight of many of Basra's leading merchants to  continued to play a significant role in Basra's commercial stagnation well into the 1850s.

The instability in Basra helped foster economic prosperity in . In the late 18th century,  was a haven for Basra merchants fleeing [[Ottoman government|Ottoman]] persecution.  was the center of [[boat building]] in the Persian Gulf, its ships renowned throughout the [[ Ocean]]. Its sailors developed a positive reputation in the Persian Gulf. In the 19th century,  became significant in the [[horse trading|horse trade]], with regular shipments in sailing vessels. In the mid 19th century, it was estimated that  exported an average of 800 horses to  annually.

In 1899, ruler Sheikh [[Mubarak Al-Sabah|Mubarak Al Sabah]] signed an agreement with the [[Presidencies and provinces of  | government in ]] (subsequently known as the [[Anglo- Agreement of 1899]]) making  a [[ protectorate]]. This gave Britain exclusive access and trade with , while denying Ottoman and  provinces to the north a port on the Persian Gulf. The [[Sheikhdom of ]] remained a  protectorate until 1961.

[[File:Basra Province 1897.png|left|thumb|The [[Basra Vilayet (Ottoman Empire)|Basra ''Vilayet'']] of the [[Ottoman Empire]] in 1897. After the [[Anglo-Ottoman Convention of 1913]],  was established as an autonomous ''[[kaza]],'' or district, of the Ottoman Empire and a ''[[de facto]]'' protectorate of [[ of Great Britain and |Great Britain]].]]
After the [[Anglo-Ottoman Convention of 1913]],  was established as an autonomous ''[[kaza]],'' or district, of the Ottoman Empire and a ''[[de facto]]'' protectorate of Great Britain.

During [[World War I]], the [[ Empire]] imposed a trade blockade against  because its ruler at the time, [[Salim Al-Mubarak Al-Sabah]], supported the [[Ottoman Empire]]. The  economic blockade heavily damaged 's economy.

In 1919, Sheikh [[Salim Al-Mubarak Al-Sabah]] intended to build a commercial city in the south of . This caused a diplomatic crisis with Najd, but Britain intervened, discouraging Sheikh Salim. In 1920, an attempt by the [[Ikhwan]] to build a stronghold in southern  led to the [[Battle of Hamdh]]. The Battle of Hamdh involved 2,000 [[Ikhwan]] fighters against 100  [[cavalrymen]] and 200  [[infantrymen]]. The battle lasted for six days and resulted in heavy but unknown casualties on both sides resulting in the victory of the Ikhwan forces and leading to the battle of Jahra around the  Red Fort. The [[Battle of Jahra]] happened as the result of the [[Battle of Hamdh]]. A force of three to four thousand [[Ikhwan]], led by [[Faisal Al-Dawish]], attacked the [[ Red Fort|Red Fort]] at Al-Jahra, defended by fifteen hundred men. The fort was besieged and the  position precarious. The Ikhwan attack repulsed for the while, negotiations began between Salim and Al-Dawish; the latter threatened another attack if the  forces did not surrender. The local merchant class convinced Salim to call in help from  troops, who showed up with airplanes and three warships, ending the attacks. After the Battle of Jahra, Ibn Saud's warriors, the [[Ikhwan]], demanded that  follows five rules. They demanded that all the [[Shias]] be evicted, that all should adopt the [[Wahhabism|Ikhwan doctrine]], that the Turks be labelled "[[heretics]]", that smoking, [[Munkar and Nakir|munkar]], and prostitution be abolished, and that  missionary hospital be destroyed.

[[File:Jahra-castle.jpg|thumb|The [[ Red Fort]] in [[Al Jahra]]]]
The [[–Najd War]] of 1919–20 erupted in the [[aftermath of World War I]]. The war occurred because [[Ibn Saud]] of Najd wanted to annex . The sharpened conflict between  and Najd led to the death of hundreds of . The war resulted in sporadic border clashes throughout 1919–1920.

When [[Percy Cox]] was informed of the border clashes in , he sent a letter to the [[Emirate of Arabistan|Ruler of Arabistan]] Sheikh [[Khazʽal Ibn Jabir]] offering the  throne to either him or one of his heirs. Khaz'al refused. He then asked: {{blockquote|...even so, do you think that you have come to me with something new? Al Mubarak's position as ruler of  means that I am the true ruler of . So there is no difference between myself and them, for they are like the dearest of my children and you are aware of this. Had someone else come to me with this offer, I would have complained about them to you. So how do you come to me with this offer when you are well aware that myself and Al Mubarak are one soul and one house, what affects them affects me, whether good or evil.}}

Following the –Najd War in 1919–20, Ibn Saud imposed a trade blockade against  from the years 1923 until 1937. The goal of the  economic and military attacks on  was to annex as much of 's territory as possible. At the [[Uqair Protocol of 1922|Uqair conference]] in 1922, the boundaries of  and Najd were set; as a result of  interference,  had no representative at the Uqair conference. After the Uqair conference,  was still subjected to a  economic blockade and intermittent  [[Raid (military)|raiding]].

 immensely declined in regional economic importance, due to the trade blockades and the world economic depression. Before [[Mary Bruins Allison]] visited  in 1934,  had already lost its prominence in long-distance trade.

[[File:Kuwait1944.jpg|thumb|upright=1.15|left|Celebration at [[Seif Palace]] in 1944]]
The [[Great Depression]] harmed 's economy, starting in the late 1920s. International trading was one of 's main sources of income before oil. 's merchants were mostly intermediary merchants. As a result of the decline of European demand for goods from  and Africa, 's economy suffered. The decline in international trade resulted in an increase in gold smuggling by 's ships to . Some local merchant families became rich from this smuggling. 's [[pearl]] industry also collapsed as a result of the worldwide economic depression. At its height, 's pearl industry had led the world's luxury market, regularly sending out between 750 and 800 ships to meet the European elite's desire for pearls. During the economic depression, luxuries like pearls were in little demand. The  invention of [[cultured pearl]]s also contributed to the collapse of 's pearl industry.

[[Freya Stark]] wrote about the extent of poverty in  at the time:{{blockquote|Poverty has settled in  more heavily since my last visit five years ago, both by sea, where the pearl trade continues to decline, and by land, where the blockade established by  now harms the merchants.}}

On 22 February 1938, [[Petroleum|oil]] was first discovered in the [[Burgan field]].

===1946–1980: State-building===
Between 1946 and 1980,  experienced a period of prosperity driven by oil and its liberal cultural atmosphere; this period is called the "golden era of ". In 1946, crude oil was exported for the first time. In 1950, a major public-work programme began to enable  citizens to enjoy a luxurious standard of living.

By 1952, the country became the largest oil exporter in the Persian Gulf region. This massive growth attracted many foreign workers, especially from , , , and  – with the latter being particularly political within the context of the [[Arab Cold War]]. It was also in 1952 that the first masterplan of  was designed by the  planning firm of [[Anthony Minoprio|Minoprio]], [[Hugh Spencely|Spenceley]], and Macfarlane. In 1958, ''[[Al-Arabi (magazine)|Al-Arabi]]'' magazine was first published. Many foreign writers moved to  because they enjoyed greater [[freedom of expression]] than elsewhere in the Middle East. 's press was described as one of the [[Freedom of the press|freest in the world]].  was the pioneer of the post-[[Nahda]] literary renaissance in the Middle East.

In June 1961,  became independent with the end of the [[Sheikhdom of #History as a Protected State of Britain| protectorate]] and the Sheikh [[Abdullah Al-Salim Al-Sabah]] became [[Emir of ]]. 's [[Public holidays in |national day]], however, is celebrated on 25 February, the anniversary of the coronation of Sheikh Abdullah (it was originally celebrated on 19 June, the date of independence, but concerns over the summer heat caused the government to move it).

At the time,  was considered the most developed country in the region.  was the pioneer in the Middle East in diversifying its earnings away from oil exports. The [[ Investment Authority]] is the world's first sovereign wealth fund.

 society embraced liberal and non-traditional attitudes throughout the 1960s and 1970s. For example, most  women did not wear the [[hijab]] in the 1960s and 70s.

[[File:HMS Victorious (R38) aerial c1959.jpeg|thumb| [[HMS Victorious (R38)|HMS ''Victorious'']] taking part in [[Operation Vantage]] in July 1961]]
Although  formally gained independence in 1961,  initially refused to recognize the country's independence by maintaining that  is part of , albeit  later briefly backed down following a show of force by Britain and [[Arab League]] support of 's independence.

The short-lived [[Operation Vantage]] crisis evolved in July 1961, as the  government threatened to invade  and the invasion was finally averted following plans by the Arab League to form an international Arab force against the potential  invasion of . As a result of Operation Vantage, the Arab League took over the border security of  and the  had withdrawn their forces by 19 October.  prime minister [[Abd al-Karim Qasim]] was killed in a coup in 1963 but, although  recognised  independence and the military threat was perceived to be reduced, Britain continued to monitor the situation and kept forces available to protect  until 1971. There had been no  military action against  at the time: this was attributed to the political and military situation within  which continued to be unstable.

A treaty of friendship between  and  was signed in 1963 by which  recognised the 1932 border of . Under the terms of the newly drafted [[Constitution of |Constitution]],  held its first [[ parliamentary election, 1963|parliamentary elections in 1963]].

[[ University]] was established in 1966. 's [[#Television and theatre|theatre industry]] became well known throughout the region. After the 1967 [[Six Day War]],  along with other Arabic speaking countries voted the three no's of the [[Khartoum Resolution]]: no peace with , no recognition of , and no negotiations with . From the 1970s onward,  scored highest of all Arab countries on the [[Human Development Index]]. The  poet [[Ahmed Matar]] left  in the 1970s to take refuge in the more liberal environment of .  is the 25th most peaceful country in the world, according to the 2024 [[Global Peace Index]].

The [[- 1973 Sanita border skirmish|- 1973 Samita border skirmish]] evolved on 20 March 1973, when  army units occupied El-Samitah near the  border, which evoked an international crisis.

On 6 February 1974, [[1974 attack on the  Embassy in | militants occupied the  embassy in ]], taking the ambassador and ten others hostage. The militants' motive was to support the [[ Red Army]] members and  militants who were holding hostages on a  ferry in what is known as the [[Laju incident|''Laju'' incident]]. Ultimately, the hostages were released, and the guerrillas allowed to fly to [[Aden]]. This was the first time  guerrillas struck in  as the Al Sabah ruling family, headed by Sheikh Sabah Al-Salim Al-Sabah, funded the  resistance movement.  had been a regular endpoint for  [[aircraft hijacking|plane hijacking]] in the past and had considered itself safe.

[[ International Airport]] was opened in 1979 by the Al Hani Construction with a joint venture of [[Ballast Nedam]].

===1981–1991: Wars and terrorism===
{{main|1983–1988  terror attacks|Gulf War}}
The Al Sabah strongly advocated [[Islamism]] throughout the 1980s. At that time, the most serious threat to the continuity of Al Sabah came from home-grown democrats, who were protesting the [[ general election, 1975|1976 suspension of the parliament]]. The Al Sabah were attracted to Islamists preaching the virtues of a [[hierarchical]] order that included loyalty to the  monarchy. In 1981, the  government [[gerrymandered]] electoral districts in favour of the Islamists. Islamists were the government's main allies, hence Islamists were able to dominate state agencies, such as the [[government ministries]].

[[File:BrennendeOelquellenKuwait1991.jpg|thumb|left|[[ oil fires]] set by retreating  forces in 1991]]
During the [[– War]],  ardently supported . As a result, there were [[1983–1988  terror attacks|various pro- terror attacks]] across , including the 1983 bombings, the attempted assassination of [[Jaber Al-Ahmad Al-Sabah|Emir Jaber]] in May 1985, the [[1985  City bombings]], and the hijacking of several  Airways planes. 's economy and scientific research sector significantly suffered due to the pro- terror attacks.

Simultaneously,  experienced a major [[economic crisis]] after the [[Souk Al-Manakh stock market crash]] and [[1980s oil glut|decrease in oil price]].

[[File:Tankskuwait.jpg|thumb|left|[[ Armed Forces]] tanks in [[ City]] of -occupied  on 2 August 1990 during the [[ invasion of ]] that began the Gulf War.]]

After the – War ended,  declined an  request to forgive its US$65&nbsp;billion debt. An economic rivalry between the two countries ensued after  increased its oil production by 40 percent. Tensions between the two countries increased further in July 1990, after  complained to [[OPEC]] claiming that  was stealing its oil from a field near the border by [[slant drilling]] of the [[Rumaila field]].

In August 1990,  forces [[Invasion of |invaded and annexed]]  without any warning. After a series of failed diplomatic negotiations, the  led a coalition to remove the  forces from , in what became known as the [[Gulf War]]. On 26 February 1991, in phase of code-named [[Operation Desert Storm]], the coalition succeeded in driving out the  forces. As they retreated,  forces carried out a [[ oil fires|scorched earth]] policy by setting oil wells on fire.

During the  occupation, nearly 1,000 civilians were killed in . In addition, 600 people went missing during 's occupation; remains of approximately 375 were found in mass graves in .  celebrates 26 February as [[Liberation Day ()|Liberation Day]].

===1992–present: Present era===
{{see also| and state-sponsored terrorism}}
In the early 1990s,  [[ exodus from  (Gulf War)|deported]] nearly 400,000 . 's policy was a form of [[collective punishment]], in response to the alignment of the [[PLO]] with Saddam Hussein.  also deported thousands of  and  after the Gulf War. Hundreds of thousands of [[Bedoon|stateless Bedoon]] were also expelled from  in the early-to-mid 1990s. At the [[House of Commons of the ]] in 1995, it was revealed that the Al Sabah ruling family deported 150,000 stateless Bedoon to refugee camps in the  desert near the  border with minimal water, insufficient food, and no basic shelter. Many of the stateless Bedoon fled to  where they remain stateless people even today.

In March 2003,  became the springboard for the US-led [[invasion of ]]. In 2005, women won the right to vote and run in elections. Upon the death of the Emir Jaber in January 2006, Sheikh [[Saad Al-Sabah]] succeeded him but was removed nine days later due to his failing health. As a result, Sheikh [[Sabah Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah]] was sworn in as Emir. From that point onwards,  suffered from chronic political deadlock between the government and parliament which resulted in multiple cabinet reshuffles and dissolutions. This significantly hampered investment and economic reforms in , making the country's economy much more dependent on oil.

Despite the political instability,  had the highest [[Human Development Index]] ranking in the Arab world from 2006 to 2009.  awarded  Investment Authority an additional $700 million quota on top of $300 million awarded in March 2012. The quota is the highest to be granted by  to foreign investment entities.

[[File: Towers in night time by ©lensofasif,  City.jpg|thumb|[[ Towers]]]]
[[File:صورة جوية لمبنى مجلس الامة.jpg|thumb| City nightscape, with the [[ National Assembly]] visible (illuminated white building in center)]]
In March 2014,  [[David S. Cohen (attorney)|David S. Cohen]], who was then the  [[Under Secretary of the Treasury for Terrorism and Financial Intelligence|Secretary of the Treasury for Terrorism and Financial Intelligence]], and many others accused [[ and state-sponsored terrorism| of funding terrorism]], particularly for [[ISIS]] and [[Al-Qaeda]].

On 26 June 2015, a [[2015  mosque bombing|suicide bombing took place]] at a Shia Muslim mosque in . The [[Islamic State of  and the Levant]] claimed responsibility for the attack. Twenty-seven people were killed and 227 people were wounded. It was the largest terror attack in 's history. In the aftermath, a lawsuit was filed accusing the  government of negligence and direct responsibility for the terror attack.

Due to [[2010s oil glut|declining oil prices]] in the mid-to-late 2010s,  faced one of the worst economic crunches in its history. [[Sabah Al Ahmad Sea City]] was inaugurated in mid-2016. Simultaneously,  invested significantly in its economic relations with [[]].  has been 's largest trade partner since 2016.

Under the [[Belt and Road Initiative]],  and  have various cooperation projects including [[Al-Mutlaa]] which is currently under construction in northern . The [[Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Al-Sabah Causeway]] is part of the first phase of the [[Madinat al-Hareer|Silk City]] project. The causeway was inaugurated in May 2019 as part of  Vision 2035, it connects  City to northern .

The [[COVID-19 pandemic in |COVID-19 pandemic]] exacerbated 's economic crisis. 's economy faced a budget deficit of $46 billion in 2020. It was 's first fiscal deficit since 1995. In September 2020, 's Crown Prince Sheikh [[Nawaf Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah]] became the 16th Emir of  and the successor to Emir Sheikh Sabah Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah, who died at the age of 91. In October 2020, Sheikh [[Mishal Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah]] was appointed as the Crown Prince. In December 2023, 's Emir Sheikh Nawaf al-Ahmad al-Jaber al-Sabah died and was replaced by Mishal Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah''.''

 currently has the largest US military presence in the entire Middle East region. There are over 14,000 US military personnel stationed in the country. [[Camp Arifjan]] is the largest US military base in . The US uses bases in  as staging hubs, training ranges, and logistical support for its Middle East operations.

In recent years, 's infrastructure projects market has regularly underperformed due to political deadlock between the executive and legislative branches.  is now the region's most oil-dependent country with the lowest share of economic diversification. According to the World Economic Forum,  has the weakest infrastructure quality in the region.

Since March 2024,  has been [[Human rights in #Citizenship revocation|revoking the citizenship]] of many citizens (by decree). By March 2025,  revoked the citizenship of 42,000 people in just six months. The most high-profile revocation was that of singer [[Nawal El Kuwaitia|Nawal]] and actor Dawood Hussain in early December 2024. According to ''[[Carnegie Endowment for International Peace|Carnegie Endowment]]'',  has weaponized citizenship revocation as a tool for political control.
==History==
{{Main|History of }}

===Prehistory===
{{Main|Prehistoric }}
[[File:Vendel I helmet 456057.jpg|thumb|A [[Vendel Period|Vendel-era]] helmet, at the  Museum of National Antiquities]]
's prehistory begins in the [[Allerød oscillation]], a warm period around 12,000 BC, with Late [[Palaeolithic]] [[reindeer]]-hunting camps of the [[Bromme culture]] at the edge of the ice in what is now the country's southernmost province, [[Scania]]. This period was characterised by small clans of [[hunter-gatherer]]s who relied on [[flint]] technology.

 and its people were first described by the Roman historian [[Publius Cornelius Tacitus]] in his ''[[Germania (book)|Germania]]'' (98 AD). In [[s:Germania#XLIV|''Germania'' 44 and 45]] he mentions the Swedes (''Suiones'') as a powerful tribe with ships that had a [[prow]] at each end ([[longship]]s). Which kings ({{Lang|gem-x-proto|kuningaz}}) ruled these Suiones is unknown, but [[Norse mythology]] presents a long line of legendary and semi-legendary kings going back to the last centuries BC. The [[Runes|runic script]] was in use among the south Scandinavian elite by at least the second century AD, but all that has survived from the Roman Period is curt inscriptions demonstrating that the people of south Scandinavia spoke [[Proto-Norse]] at the time, a language ancestral to  and other [[North Germanic languages]].

In the sixth century, the Byzantine historian [[Jordanes]] names two tribes living in [[Scandza]], both of which are now considered to be synonymous with the Swedes: the {{Lang|la|Suetidi}} and {{Lang|la|Suehans}}. The {{Lang|la|Suehans}} were known to the Roman world as suppliers of black fox skins and, according to Jordanes, had very fine horses, similar to those of the ''[[Thuringians|Thyringi]]'' of {{Lang|la|Germania}} ("{{Lang|la|alia vero gens ibi moratur Suehans, quae velud Thyringi equis utuntur eximiis}}").

===Viking Age===
{{See also|Early  history|Consolidation of |Varangians}}
[[File:Vikings-Voyages.png|upright=1.3|thumb|left|[[Viking]] expeditions (blue lines)]]

The  [[Viking Age]] lasted roughly from the eighth century to the 11th century. It is believed that  Vikings and [[Gutes|Gutar]] mainly travelled east and south, going to , , the [[Baltic countries]], , , , the [[Black Sea]] and even as far as [[Baghdad]]. Their routes passed [[The Trade Route from the Varangians to the |through the Dnieper]] south to [[Constantinople]], on which they carried out numerous raids. The [[Byzantine Emperor|Byzantine emperor]] [[Theophilos (emperor)|Theophilos]] noticed their great skills in war and invited them to serve as his personal bodyguard, known as the [[Varangian Guard]]. The  Vikings, called [[Rus (people)|Rus]], are believed to be the founders of [[Kievan Rus']]. The Vikings were described by many outside sources, such as the Arab traveler [[Ibn Fadlan]]. The actions of these [[Vikings| Vikings]] are commemorated on many [[runestone]]s in , such as the [[ runestones]] and the [[Varangian runestones]]. There was also considerable participation in expeditions westwards, which are commemorated on stones such as the [[England runestones]]. The last major  Viking expedition appears to have been the ill-fated expedition of [[Ingvar the Far-Travelled]] to [[Serkland]], the region south-east of the [[Caspian Sea]]. Its members are commemorated on the [[Ingvar runestones]], none of which mentions any survivor.

[[File:Bildsten med skepp 800-1099 Tjängvide, Gotland.jpg|thumb|The [[Tjängvide image stone]] dating from 800 to 1099, example of Viking art]]

During the early stages of the Viking Age, a centre of trade in [[Northern Europe]] developed at [[Birka]] on the island of [[Björkö, Ekerö|Björkö]], not far from where Stockholm was later constructed, in mid-latitude . Birka was founded around 750 AD as a trading port by a king or merchants trying to control trade. Birka was the [[Baltic Sea|Baltic]] link in the [[Dnieper trade route]] through [[Staraya Ladoga|Ladoga]] (''Aldeigja'') and [[Novgorod Land|Novgorod]] (''Holmsgard'') to the [[Byzantine Empire]] and the [[Abbasid Caliphate]]. It was abandoned around 975, at about the same time [[Sigtuna]] was founded as a town some 35&nbsp;km to the northeast. It has been estimated that the population in Viking Age Birka was between 500 and 1000 people. Archaeological finds indicate that Birka still was wealthy in the 9th and 10th centuries. Thousands of graves, coins, jewelry and other luxury items have been found there.

===Kingdom of ===
[[File:Map of  ca 1280.png|thumb|right|A rough map of the extent of  rule, {{circa|1280}}]]
The exact age of the kingdom of  is unknown. Determining its age depends mostly on whether  is considered a nation when the {{Lang|sv|[[Svear]]}} (Swedes) ruled Svealand or when the {{Lang|sv|Svear}} and the {{Lang|sv|[[Götar]]}} (Geats) of Götaland were united under a single ruler. Svealand was described by [[Tacitus]] in 98 AD as being under a single ruler, though it is unknown how long this had been the case. The epic poem ''Beowulf'' describes semi-legendary [[-Geatish wars]] in the sixth century.

However, historians typically start the line of [[ monarchs]] from when Svealand and Götaland were ruled under the same king, namely [[Erik the Victorious]] and his son [[Olof Skötkonung]] in the tenth century. These events are often described as the [[consolidation of ]], although substantial areas were conquered and incorporated later. In this context, "Götaland" primarily refers to the provinces of [[Östergötland]] and [[Västergötland]]. [[Småland]] was of little interest at the time due to its deep pine forests, with only the city of [[Kalmar]] and its castle holding any significant importance. There were also  settlements along the southern coastline of [[Norrland]], one of the four [[lands of ]].

[[Ansgar| Ansgar]] is traditionally credited with introducing Christianity to  in 829, but the new religion did not begin to fully replace [[paganism]] until the 12th century. During that century,  was undergoing dynastic struggles between the [[House of Eric|Erik]] and [[House of Sverker|Sverker]] clans. The conflict ended when a third clan married into the Erik clan, founding the [[House of Bjälbo|Bjälbo]] dynasty, which gradually consolidated  into a stronger state. According to the ''Legend of [[ Erik]]'' and the ''[[Erik's Chronicle]]'',  kings conducted [[ Crusades (disambiguation)|a series of Crusades]] to pagan  and started conflicts with the [[Kievan Rus'|Rus']], who by then had no further connections with . As a result of the Crusades, mostly with the Second  Crusade led by [[Birger Jarl]]  gradually became part of the kingdom of  and the sphere of influence of the [[Catholic Church]]. The Swedes built fortresses in [[Häme|Tavastland]] and [[Åbo]], while a  royal council was instituted, an administrative structure and fiscal apparatus was created, and law codes were codified during the reigns of [[Magnus Ladulås]] (1275–1290) and [[Magnus Eriksson]] (1319–1364). As a result, the  lands were firmly integrated into the  realm.

Except for the provinces of Scania, Blekinge, and Halland in the southwest of the Scandinavian peninsula, which were part of the Kingdom of  during this period, [[feudalism]] never developed in  as it did in much of Europe. As a result, the peasantry remained largely a class of free farmers throughout most of  history. [[Slavery]], also known as [[thrall]]dom, was not common in , and the institution gradually diminished due to the spread of Christianity, the difficulty of obtaining slaves from lands east of the Baltic Sea, and by the development of cities before the 16th century. Indeed, both slavery and [[serfdom]] were abolished altogether by a decree of King [[Magnus Eriksson]] in 1335.  remained a poor and economically underdeveloped country, where barter was the primary means of exchange.

In 1319,  and  were united in a [[personal union]] under King Magnus Eriksson, the grandson of King [[Magnus Ladulås]] of  and of King [[Haakon V of |Haakon V]] of . Magnus Eriksson also ruled Scania from 1332 to 1360. In the mid-14th century,  was struck by the [[Black Death]]. The population of  and most of Europe was decimated. The population did not reach its pre-1348 levels until the beginning of the 19th century, with one third of the population dying between 1349 and 1351. During this period, the cities began to acquire greater rights and were heavily influenced by  merchants of the [[Hanseatic League]], active especially at [[Visby]]. In 1397, Queen [[Margaret I of ]] (the former daughter-in-law of Magnus Eriksson) established the personal union of , , and  through the [[Kalmar Union]]. However, Margaret's successors, whose rule was centred in , were unable to control the  nobility.

[[File:Gustav Vasa.jpg|thumb|left|upright|[[Gustav I of |Gustav I]] [[ War of Liberation|liberated]]  from [[Christian II of ]], ending the [[Kalmar Union]]. He established the [[House of Vasa]] which ruled  and  until the 17th century.]]

In 1520, King [[Christian II of ]], who attempted to restore the Union of Kalmar through military force, ordered the massacre of  nobles in Stockholm, an event known as the "[[Stockholm Bloodbath]]." This atrocity incited the  nobility to renew their resistance, and on 6 June 1523 (now celebrated as [[National Day of |'s National Day]]), they made [[Gustav Vasa]] their king. This is sometimes considered as the [[foundation of modern ]]. Shortly afterwards the new king rejected Catholicism and led  into the [[Protestant Reformation]]. The term {{Lang|sv|riksdag}} was used for the first time in the 1540s, although the first meeting where representatives of different social groups were called to discuss and determine affairs affecting the country as a whole took place as early as 1435, in the town of [[Arboga]]. During the [[Riksdag of the Estates|Riksdag assemblies]] of 1527 and 1544, under King Gustav Vasa, representatives of all four [[estates of the realm]] (clergy, [[ nobility|nobility]], [[Bourgeoisie|townsmen]] and [[peasant]]s) were called on to participate for the first time. The monarchy became hereditary in 1544. When Gustav Vasa broke the monopoly power of the [[Hanseatic League]], he was regarded as a hero by the  people. Furthermore, when  became more developed, after breaking the trade monopoly of the Hanseatic League, and entered its golden age, the fact that the peasantry had traditionally been free meant that a greater share of the economic benefits went to them rather than to a feudal landowning class.

The end of the 16th century was marked by a final phase of rivalry between the remaining Catholics and the new Protestant communities. In 1592, Gustav Vasa's Catholic grandson and [[king of ]], [[Sigismund III Vasa|Sigismund]], ascended the  throne. He pursued to strengthen [[Holy See|Rome]]'s influence by initiating [[Counter-Reformation]] and created a dual monarchy that temporarily became known as the [[- Union]]. His despotic rule, strongly characterised by intolerance towards the Protestants, sparked a [[War against Sigismund|civil war]] that plunged  into poverty. In opposition, Sigismund's uncle and successor, [[Charles IX of |Charles Vasa]], summoned the [[Uppsala Synod]] in 1593 which officially confirmed the modern [[Church of ]] as [[Lutheranism|Lutheran]]. Following his [[deposition (politics)|deposition]] in 1599, Sigismund attempted to reclaim the throne sparing no expense, and hostilities between [[– Commonwealth|]] and  continued for the next hundred years.

=== Empire===
{{See also|History of  (1611–1648)| Empire| overseas colonies|Age of Liberty|Gustavian era|Union between  and }}
[[File:Gustave Adolphe at Breitenfeld-Johann Walter-f3706497.jpg|thumb|[[Gustavus Adolphus of |Gustavus Adolphus]] at the [[Battle of Breitenfeld (1631)|Battle of Breitenfeld]] in 1631]]
[[File: Empire.svg|thumb|The [[ Empire]] between 1560 and 1815; its peak was between 1658 and 1660]]
 rose to prominence on a continental scale during the reign of king [[Gustavus Adolphus of |Gustavus Adolphus]], seizing territories from [[Tsardom of |]] and the [[– Commonwealth]] in multiple conflicts.{{sfn|Frost|2000|p=102}} During the Thirty Years' War,  conquered approximately half of the Holy Roman states and defeated the Imperial army at the [[Battle of Breitenfeld (1631)|Battle of Breitenfeld]] in 1631.{{sfn|Frost|2000|p=103}} Gustavus Adolphus planned to become the new [[Holy Roman Emperor]], ruling over a united Scandinavia and the Holy Roman states, but he was killed at the [[Battle of Lützen (1632)|Battle of Lützen]] in 1632. After the [[Battle of Nördlingen (1634)|Battle of Nördlingen]] in 1634 – 's only significant military defeat of the war – pro- sentiment among the  states faded.{{sfn|Frost|2000|p=103}} These  provinces broke away from  power one by one, leaving  with only a few northern  territories: [[ Pomerania]], [[Bremen-Verden]] and [[Wismar]]. From 1643 to 1645, during the last years of the war,  and [[-]] fought the [[Torstenson War]]. The result of that conflict and the conclusion of the Thirty Years' War helped establish postwar  as a major force in Europe.{{sfn|Frost|2000|p=103}} The [[Peace of Westphalia]] in 1648 granted  territories in northern .

In the middle of the 17th century,  was the third-largest country in Europe by land area.  reached its largest territorial extent under the rule of [[Charles X of |Charles X]] after the [[treaty of Roskilde]] in 1658, following Charles X's [[March Across the Belts|crossing of the  Belts]]. The foundation of 's success during this period is credited to Gustav I's major changes to the [[Economy of | economy]] in the 16th century, and his introduction of [[Protestantism]]. One-third of the  population died in the devastating [[Great Famine of 1695–1697]] that struck the country. Famine also hit , killing roughly 10% of 's population.

In the 17th century,  was engaged in many wars, for example with –, with both sides competing for territories of today's [[Baltic states]]. The – War (1626–1629) ended with a ceasefire in [[Stary Targ]] ([[Truce of Altmark]]) on 26 September 1629 that was in favour of the Swedes, to whom  ceded the larger part of [[Livonia]] together with its important port of [[Riga]]. The Swedes also gained the right to tax ’s Baltic trade (3.5% on the value of goods), and kept control of several cities in [[Royal Prussia]] and [[Ducal Prussia]] (including [[Pillau]] (Baltiysk), [[Klaipėda|Memel]] (Klaipėda) and [[Elbing]] (Elbląg)). The Swedes later conducted a series of invasions into the – Commonwealth, known as the [[Deluge (history)|Deluge]].{{sfn|Frost|2000|p=156}} After more than half a century of almost constant warfare, the  economy had deteriorated. It became the lifetime task of Charles X's son, [[Charles XI of |Charles XI]], to rebuild the economy and refit the army.{{sfn|Frost|2000|p=216}} His legacy to his son, the coming ruler of , [[Charles XII of |Charles XII]], was one of the finest arsenals in the world, a large standing army and a great fleet.{{sfn|Frost|2000|p=222}} , the most serious threat to  at this time, had a larger army but lagged far behind in both equipment and training.{{sfn|Frost|2000|p=232}}

After the [[Battle of Narva (1700)|Battle of Narva]] in 1700, one of the first battles of the [[Great Northern War]], the  army was so severely devastated that  had an open chance to invade .{{sfn|Frost|2000|p=230}} However, Charles XII did not pursue the  army, instead [[ invasion of  (1701–1706)|turning against ]] and defeating the  king, [[Augustus II the Strong]], and his Saxon allies at the [[Battle of Kliszów]] in 1702.{{sfn|Frost|2000|p=272}} This gave  time to rebuild and modernise its army.

[[File:Marten's Poltava.jpg|thumb|right|The [[Battle of Poltava]] in 1709. In the following years,  and her allies occupied all [[Dominions of | dominions]] on the Baltic coast and even .]]

After the success of invading , Charles XII decided to make an attempt at [[ invasion of |invading ]], but this ended in a decisive  victory at the [[Battle of Poltava]] in 1709.{{sfn|Frost|2000|p=290}} After a long march exposed to [[Cossack]] raids, the  Tsar [[Peter the Great]]'s [[scorched-earth]] techniques and [[Great Frost of 1709|the extremely cold winter of 1709]], the Swedes stood weakened with a shattered morale and were enormously outnumbered against the  army at Poltava.{{sfn|Frost|2000|p=286}} The defeat meant the beginning of the end for the  Empire. In addition, [[The plague during the Great Northern War|the plague raging in East Central Europe]] devastated the [[ dominions]] and reached Central  in 1710. Returning to  in 1715, Charles XII launched [[Great Northern War and |two campaigns against ]] in 1716 and 1718, respectively. During the second attempt, he was shot to death during the [[siege of Fredriksten]] fortress.{{sfn|Frost|2000|p=295}} The Swedes were not militarily defeated at Fredriksten, but the whole structure and organisation of the campaign fell apart with the king's death. Forced to cede large areas of land in the [[Treaty of Nystad]] in 1721,  also lost its place as an empire and as the dominant state on the Baltic Sea.{{sfn|Frost|2000|p=296}} With 's lost influence,  emerged as an empire and became one of [[European balance of power|Europe's dominant nations]]. As the war finally ended in 1721,  had lost an estimated 200,000 men, 150,000 of those from the area of present-day  and 50,000 from the [[ under  rule| part of ]].
Executive power was historically shared between the King and an aristocratic [[Privy council]] until 1680, followed by the King's [[autocracy|autocratic rule]] initiated by the commoner estates of the [[Riksdag]]. As a reaction to the failed Great Northern War, a parliamentary system was introduced in 1719, followed by three different flavours of constitutional monarchy in 1772, 1789 and 1809, [[ constitution of 1809|the latter]] granting several civil liberties. Already during the first of those three periods, the 'Era of Liberty' (1719–72) the  Riksdag had developed into a very active parliament, and this tradition continued into the nineteenth century, laying the basis for the transition towards modern democracy at the end of that century.
In the 18th century,  did not have enough resources to maintain its territories outside Scandinavia, and most of them were lost, culminating with [[ War|the loss in 1809]] of eastern  to , which became the highly autonomous [[Grand Duchy of |Grand Principality of ]] in [[ Empire|Imperial ]].

In interest of re-establishing  dominance in the Baltic Sea,  allied itself against its traditional ally and benefactor, , in the [[Napoleonic Wars]]. However, in 1810, a  Marshal, [[Jean-Baptiste Bernadotte]], was chosen as heir presumptive to [[Charles XIII]]; in 1818, he established the [[House of Bernadotte]], taking the [[regnal name]] of Charles XIV. 's role in the [[Battle of Leipzig]] gave it the authority to force –, an ally of , to cede  to the King of  on 14 January 1814 in exchange for the northern  provinces, at the [[Treaty of Kiel]]. The  attempts to keep their status as a sovereign state were rejected by the  king, [[Charles XIII]]. He launched a [[– War (1814)|military campaign against ]] on 27 July 1814, ending in the [[Convention of Moss]], which forced  into a [[Union between  and |personal union]] with  under the  crown, which lasted until 1905. The 1814 campaign was the last time  was at war.

===Modern history===
{{See also|Modernization of | emigration to the }}
[[File:Starvation image from Fäderneslandet 1867.jpg|thumb|Starvation in northern  depicted in an illustration of the [[ famine of 1867–1869|Famine of 1867–1869]]]]
[[File:Farewell_to_home,_Göteborg,_1905_(cropped).jpg|thumb| emigrants boarding a ship in [[Gothenburg]] in 1905]]
The [[ East  Company]] began in 1731. The obvious choice of home port was [[Gothenburg]] ({{langx|sv|Göteborg}}) at 's west coast, as the mouth of [[Göta älv|Göta älv river]] was very wide and had the county's largest and best harbour for high-seas journeys. The trade continued into the 19th century, and caused the little town to become 's second city.
Between 1750 and 1850, the population in  doubled. According to some scholars, mass emigration to America became the only way to prevent famine and rebellion; over 1% of the population emigrated annually during the 1880s. It is thought that between 1850 and 1910 more than one million [[ emigration to the |Swedes moved to the ]]. Nevertheless,  remained poor, retaining a nearly entirely agricultural economy even as Western European countries began to industrialise.

Despite the slow rate of industrialisation into the 19th century, many important changes were taking place in the agrarian economy due to constant innovations and a rapid population growth. These innovations included government-sponsored programmes of [[enclosure]], aggressive exploitation of agricultural lands, and the introduction of new crops such as the potato. The  farming culture began to take on a critical role in  politics, which has continued through modern times with modern Agrarian party (now called the Centre Party). Between 1870 and 1914,  began developing the industrialised economy that exists today.

Strong grassroots movements sprang up in  during the latter half of the 19th century (trade unions, [[temperance movement|temperance]] groups, and independent religious groups), creating a strong foundation of democratic principles. These movements precipitated 's migration into a modern parliamentary democracy, achieved by the time of World War I. As the [[Industrial Revolution]] progressed during the 20th century, people gradually moved into cities to work in factories and became involved in socialist unions. A communist revolution was avoided in 1917, following the re-introduction of [[parliamentarism]], and the country was [[Democracy|democratised]].

===World War I and World War II===
{{Main| during World War I| during World War II}}

 was officially neutral during [[World War I]]. However, under pressure from the [[ Empire]], they did take steps which were detrimental to the [[Allies of World War I|Allied powers]] – most notably, mining the [[Öresund]] channel, thus closing it to Allied shipping, and allowing the  to use  facilities and the  [[cipher]] to transmit secret messages to their overseas embassies.  also allowed volunteers to fight alongside the  for the [[White Guard ()|White Guards]] against the [[Red Guards ()|Red Guards]] and  in the [[ Civil War]], and briefly occupied [[Åland]] in cooperation with the  Empire.

As in the First World War,  remained officially neutral during [[World War II]], although its neutrality has been disputed.  was under  influence for much of the war, as ties to the rest of the world were cut off through blockades.<!---Koblik, pg. 307. "Through the blockade of foreign trade that culminated in the establishment of the [[Skagerrak]] blockade in connection with the  invasion of  and  in April 1940,  imports were reduced by approximately one-half and exports by about one-third in comparison with the average volume of 1936–1938."---> The  government unofficially supported  in the [[Winter War]] and the [[Continuation War]] by allowing volunteers and [[materiel]] to be shipped to . However,  supported  resistance against , and in 1943 helped [[Rescue of the  Jews|rescue  Jews]] from deportation to [[Nazi concentration camps]].

During the last year of the war,  began to play a role in humanitarian efforts, and many refugees, among them several thousand Jews from Nazi-occupied Europe, were rescued thanks to the [[White Buses| rescue missions to internment camps]] and partly because  served as a haven for refugees.<!---Nordstrom, p. 317: "In the last year of the war,  became a factor in humanitarian efforts and attempts to end the war. It also became a haven for refugees from ''Norden'' and the Baltic states, and Swedes were involved in rescuing Scandinavian victims of internment camps." --- Nordstrom, p. 318: "By late 1943  was a haven for some 11,000 refugees from , including over 7,000  Jews, and about 30,000 ."---> The  diplomat [[Raoul Wallenberg]] and his colleagues ensured the safety of tens of thousands of  Jews. Nevertheless, both Swedes and others have argued that  could have done more to oppose the Nazis' war efforts.

===Post-war era===
[[File:Olivecrona erlander 380.jpg|thumb|[[Tage Erlander]] (left), Prime Minister under the ruling [[ Social Democratic Party]] from 1946 to 1969]]
 was officially a neutral country and remained outside [[NATO]] and [[Warsaw Pact]] membership during the [[Cold War]], but privately 's leadership had strong ties with the  and other western governments. Following the war,  took advantage of an intact industrial base, social stability and its natural resources to expand its industry to supply the rebuilding of Europe.<!---Recovery from the material damage and economic shocks of the war was more rapid than many expected."--->  received aid under the [[Marshall Plan]] and participated in the OECD. During most of the post-war era, the country was governed by the [[ Social Democratic Party]] largely in co-operation with [[ Trade Union Confederation|trade unions]] and industry. The government actively pursued an internationally competitive manufacturing sector of primarily large corporations.

 was one of the founding states of the [[European Free Trade Area]] (EFTA). During the 1960s the EFTA countries were often referred to as the Outer Seven, as opposed to the [[Inner Six]] of the then-[[European Economic Community]] (EEC).

Like many industrialised countries,  entered a period of economic decline and upheaval following the oil embargoes of 1973–74 and 1978–79. In the 1980s several key  industries were significantly restructured. Shipbuilding was discontinued, wood pulp was integrated into modernised paper production, the steel industry was concentrated and specialised, and mechanical engineering was robotised.  GDP per capita ranking declined during this time.

===Recent history===
{{See also|History of  (1991–present)}}
A bursting real estate bubble caused by inadequate controls on lending combined with an international recession and a policy switch from anti-unemployment policies to anti-inflationary policies resulted in a [[ financial crisis 1990-1994|fiscal crisis]] in the early 1990s. 's GDP declined by around 5%. In 1992, a run on the currency caused the central bank to briefly increase interest rates to 500%.

[[File:Tratado de Lisboa 13 12 2007 (081).jpg|thumb|right| joined the European Union in 1995, and signed the [[Lisbon Treaty]] in 2007.]]
The response of the government was to cut spending and institute a multitude of reforms to improve 's competitiveness, among them reducing the [[welfare state]] and [[Privatisation|privatising]] public services and goods. [[1994  European Union membership referendum|A referendum]] passed with 52.3% in favour of joining the EU on 13 November 1994.  joined the [[European Union]] on 1 January 1995. In a 2003 referendum the  electorate [[2003  euro referendum|voted against]] joining the [[European Monetary Union|Euro]] currency.  held the chair of the European Union from 1 July to 31 December 2009.

On 28 September 1994, the [[Sinking of the MS |MS  sank]] as the ship was crossing the Baltic Sea, en route from Tallinn, , to Stockholm, . The disaster claimed the lives of 852 people (501 of them were Swedes), being one of the worst maritime disasters of the 20th century.

Until 2022,  generally remained non-aligned militarily, although it participated in some joint military exercises with the [[North Atlantic Treaty Organization]] (NATO) and some other countries, stationed its troops under NATO command in [[Islamic Republic of |]], took part in EU-sponsored [[peacekeeping]] operations in [[Kosovo]], [[]], and [[]], and [[2011 military intervention in |helped enforce]] a [[United Nations Security Council Resolution 1973|UN-mandated no-fly zone]] over  during the [[Arab Spring]]. In addition, there was extensive cooperation with other European countries in the area of defence technology and defence industry; some -made weaponry was used by [[Multi-National Force – |Coalition]] militaries in . In response to the [[2022  invasion of ]],  moved to formally join NATO, alongside . After many months of delays caused by the objections of  and ,  became a NATO member on 7 March 2024.

In recent decades  has become a more culturally diverse nation due to significant immigration; in 2013, it was estimated that 15% of the population was foreign-born, and an additional 5% of the population were born to two immigrant parents. The influx of immigrants has brought new social challenges. Violent incidents have [[Rosengård#Violence|periodically occurred]] including the [[May 2013 Stockholm riots|2013 Stockholm riots]]. In response to these violent events, the [[Far-right politics|anti-immigration]] opposition party, the [[ Democrats]], promoted their anti-immigration policies, while the [[Left-wing politics|left-wing]] opposition blamed growing inequality caused by the [[Centre-right politics|centre-right]] government's socioeconomic policies.

Since the postwar period, [[LGBTQ rights in ]] have gradually expanded through the steady extension of legal and social protections for LGBTQ+ people. Over subsequent decades, anti-discrimination laws, adoption rights, and the ability to change legal gender were progressively strengthened, contributing to high levels of public support for LGBTQ+ equality. In the mid-2010s, however,  also saw the rise of [[Anti-gender movement in |anti-gender mobilizations]], which gender studies scholars situate within a broader process of [[democratic backsliding]].

 was heavily affected by the [[2015 European migrant crisis]], eventually forcing the government to tighten regulations of entry to the country. Some of the asylum restrictions were relaxed again later.

On 30 November 2021, [[Magdalena Andersson]] became 's first female prime minister. The September 2022 general [[2022  general election|election]] ended in a narrow win to a bloc of right-wing parties. On 18 October 2022, [[Ulf Kristersson]] of the Moderate Party became the new Prime Minister.
==History==
{{Main|History of }}

{{For timeline|Timeline of  history}}

=== Indigenous prehistory ===
{{Main|Prehistory of |Indigenous }}

[[File:Bradshaw rock paintings.jpg|thumb|upright=1.0|right|[[Aboriginal rock art]] in the [[Kimberley (Western )|Kimberley]] region of Western ]]

[[Indigenous ]] comprise two broad groups:
* [[Aboriginal ]], who are the various [[Indigenous peoples]] of the  mainland and many of its islands, including [[Aboriginal Tasmanians|Tasmania]]
* [[Torres Strait Islanders]], who are a distinct [[Melanesia]]n people of [[Torres Strait Islands]]

Human habitation of the  continent is estimated to have begun 50,000 to 65,000 years ago, with the migration of people by [[land bridge]]s and short sea crossings from what is now Southeast Asia. It is uncertain how many waves of immigration may have contributed to these ancestors of modern Aboriginal . The [[Madjedbebe]] rock shelter in [[Arnhem Land]] is possibly the oldest site showing the presence of humans in . The oldest human remains found are the [[Lake Mungo remains]], which have been dated to around 42,000 years ago.

Aboriginal  culture is one of the oldest continuous cultures on Earth. At the time of first European contact, Aboriginal  belonged to wide range of societies, with diverse economies spread across at least [[ Aboriginal languages|250 different language groups]]. Estimates of the Aboriginal population before  settlement range from 300,000 to 3 million. Aboriginal  cultures were (and remain) deeply connected with the land and the environment, with stories of [[The Dreaming]] maintained through [[oral tradition]], [[Songline|songs]], dance and paintings. Certain groups engaged in [[fire-stick farming]], [[fish farming]], and built [[Indigenous architecture#|semi-permanent shelters]]. These practices have variously been characterised as "[[hunter-gatherer]]", "[[Agriculture|agricultural]]", "natural cultivation" and "intensification".

Torres Strait Islander people first settled their islands at least 2,500 years ago. Culturally and linguistically distinct from mainland Aboriginal peoples, they were seafarers and obtained their livelihood from seasonal horticulture and the resources of their reefs and seas. Agriculture also developed on some islands and villages appeared by the 1300s. By the mid-18th century in northern , [[Makassan contact with |contact, trade and cross-cultural engagement]] had been established between local Aboriginal groups and [[Makassar people|Makassan]] [[trepanging|trepangers]], visiting from present-day .

===European exploration and colonisation===
{{Main|European maritime exploration of |European land exploration of |History of  (1788–1850)}}

[[File:Landing of Lieutenant James Cook at Botany Bay, 29 April 1770 (painting by E Phillips Fox).jpg|alt=Landing of Lieutenant James Cook at Botany Bay, 29 April 1770|left|thumb|Landing of [[James Cook]] at [[Botany Bay]] on 29 April 1770]]
The [[ East  Company]] ship, ''[[Duyfken]]'', captained by [[Willem Janszoon]], made the first documented European landing in  in 1606. Later that year, [[Luís Vaz de Torres]] sailed to the north of  through [[Torres Strait]], along New 's southern coast. [[Abel Tasman]]'s voyage of 1642 was the first known European expedition to reach [[Van Diemen's Land]]. On his second voyage of 1644, he mapped the north coast of  south of New . Following Tasman's voyages, the  were able to make almost complete maps of 's northern and western coasts and much of its southern and south-eastern Tasmanian coasts. They named the continent [[New Holland ()|New Holland]]''.''

In 1770, Captain [[James Cook]] sailed along and mapped the east coast, which he named "[[New South Wales]]" and claimed for Great Britain. in 1786, the  government announced its intention to establish a [[penal colony]] in New South Wales. On 26 January 1788, the [[First Fleet]] commanded by Captain [[Arthur Phillip]], arrived at [[Sydney Cove]], Port Jackson. A camp was established and the [[Union Jack|Union Flag]] raised. The date later became [[ Day|'s national day]].

Most early settlers were [[convicts in |convicts]], [[penal transportation|transported]] for petty crimes and [[convict assignment|assigned]] as labourers or servants to "free settlers" (willing immigrants). Once [[emancipist|emancipated]], convicts tended to integrate into colonial society. Aboriginal resistance, convict rebellions and [[Bushranger|bushranging]] were sometimes suppressed under martial law. The 1808 [[Rum Rebellion]], carried out by officers of the [[New South Wales Corps|New South Wales Corp]], led to a temporary [[military junta]]. During the next two decades, social and economic reforms, together with the establishment of a [[New South Wales Legislative Council|Legislative Council]] and [[Supreme Court of New South Wales|Supreme Court]], saw the penal colony transition to a civil society.

<!-- Please take note of talk page discussion (archive 21, Colonial expansion, treaties and land rights) before editing -->The indigenous population declined for 150 years following European settlement, mainly due to infectious disease.  colonial authorities did not sign any treaties with [[Aboriginal #Groups and sub-groups|Aboriginal groups]]. As settlement expanded, tens of thousands of Indigenous people and thousands of settlers were killed in [[ frontier wars|frontier conflicts]], which many historians argue included acts of [[Genocide of Indigenous |genocide]] by settlers. Settlers dispossessed surviving Indigenous peoples of most of their land.

===Colonial expansion===
{{Main|History of  (1788–1850)|History of  (1851–1900)}}

[[File:PortArthurPenitentiary.jpg|thumb|upright=1.0|right|alt=A calm body of water is in the foreground. The shoreline is about 200 metres away. To the left, close to the shore, are three tall [[Eucalyptus|gum trees]]; behind them on an incline are ruins, including walls and watchtowers of light-coloured stone and brick, what appear to be the foundations of walls, and grassed areas. To the right lie the outer walls of a large rectangular four-storey building dotted with regularly spaced windows. Forested land rises gently to a peak several kilometres back from the shore.|Tasmania's [[Port Arthur, Tasmania|Port Arthur]] penal settlement is one of eleven UNESCO World Heritage-listed [[ Convict Sites]].]]

In 1803, a settlement was established in [[Van Diemen's Land]] (present-day [[Tasmania]]), and in 1813, [[Gregory Blaxland]], [[William Lawson (explorer)|William Lawson]] and [[William Wentworth]] [[1813 crossing of the Blue Mountains|crossed the Blue Mountains]] west of Sydney, opening the interior to European settlement. The  claim was extended to the whole  continent in 1827 when Major [[Edmund Lockyer]] established a settlement on [[King George Sound]] (modern-day [[Albany, Western |Albany]]). The [[Swan River Colony]] (present-day [[Perth]]) was established in 1829, evolving into the largest  colony by area, [[History of Western |Western ]]. Separate colonies were carved from New South Wales: Tasmania in 1825, [[ colonisation of South |South ]] in 1836, [[Colony of Victoria|Victoria]] in 1851, and [[Colony of Queensland|Queensland]] in 1859. South  and Victoria were founded as free colonies—they never accepted transported convicts. Growing [[Australasian Anti-Transportation League|opposition to the convict system]] culminated in its abolition in the eastern colonies by the 1850s. Initially a free colony, Western  accepted convicts from 1850 to 1868.

The six colonies individually gained [[responsible government]] between 1855 and 1890, managing most of their own affairs while remaining part of the [[ Empire]]. The Colonial Office in London retained control of some matters, notably foreign affairs. The colonial parliaments progressively extended voting rights to adult men from 1856, with [[women's suffrage]] on equal terms following between the 1890s and 1900s. Some colonies introduced racial restrictions on voting from 1885.

In the mid-19th century, explorers such as [[Burke and Wills expedition|Burke and Wills]] charted 's interior. A [[ gold rushes|series of gold rushes]] beginning in the early 1850s led to an influx of new migrants from [[ |]], North America and continental Europe, as well as outbreaks of [[bushranger|bushranging]] and civil unrest; the latter peaked in 1854 when [[Ballarat]] miners launched the [[Eureka Rebellion]] against gold licence fees. The 1860s saw the rise of [[blackbirding]], where [[South Sea Islanders]] were coerced or abducted into [[indentured labour]], mainly by Queensland colonists.

From 1886,  colonial governments began [[Stolen Generations|removing many Aboriginal children]] from their families and communities, justified on the grounds of child protection and [[forced assimilation]] policies. The [[Second Boer War]] (1899–1902) marked the largest overseas deployment of [[colonial forces of |'s colonial forces]].

===Federation to the World Wars===
{{Main|History of  (1901–1945)}}

{{See also|Federation of |Military history of  during World War I|Military history of  during World War II}}
[[File:Opening of the first parliament.jpg|thumb|''[[The Big Picture (painting)|The Big Picture]]'', a painting by [[Tom Roberts]], depicts the opening of the first  Parliament in 1901.]]
On 1 January 1901, [[Federation of |federation of the colonies]] was achieved after a decade of planning, [[Constitutional Convention ()|constitutional conventions]] and [[1898–1900  constitutional referendums|referendums]], resulting in the establishment of the Commonwealth of  as a nation under the new [[Constitution of | Constitution]].

From 1901,  was a self-governing [[dominion]] within the  Empire. It was one of the founding members of the [[League of Nations]] in 1920, and the [[Member states of the United Nations|United Nations]] in 1945. The ''[[Statute of Westminster 1931]]'' ended the ability of the UK to legislate for  at the federal level without 's consent.  [[Statute of Westminster Adoption Act 1942|adopted it]] in 1942, but it was backdated to 1939 to confirm the validity of legislation passed during World War II.

The [[ Capital Territory]] was formed in 1911 as the location for the future federal capital of [[Canberra]]. While it was being constructed, [[Melbourne]] served as the temporary capital from 1901 to 1927. The [[Northern Territory]] was transferred from the control of South  to the Commonwealth in 1911.  took over the administration of the [[Territory of Papua]] (which had previously been a  colony) in 1905 and of the [[Territory of New ]] (formerly [[ New ]]) in 1920. The two were unified as the [[Territory of Papua and New ]] in 1949 and gained independence from  in 1975.

[[File:Darwin 42.jpg|thumb|The 1942 [[Bombing of Darwin]], the first of more than 100 [[Air raids on , 1942–1943| air raids on ]] during [[World War II]]]]
In 1914,  joined the [[Allies of World War I|Allies]] in the First World War, and took part in the fighting on several fronts. Of the 324,000 men who served overseas, about 60,000 were killed and another 152,000 were wounded. Many  regard the defeat of the [[ and  Army Corps]] (ANZAC) at [[Gallipoli Campaign|Gallipoli]] in 1915 as the "baptism of fire" that forged the [[Anzac spirit|new nation's identity]]. The [[Landing at Anzac Cove|beginning of the campaign]] is commemorated annually on [[Anzac Day]], a date which rivals [[ Day]] as the nation's most important.

From 1939 to 1945,  joined the [[Allies of World War II|Allies]] in fighting the Second World War. 's [[ Defence Force|armed forces]] fought in the [[Pacific War|Pacific]], [[European Theatre of World War II|European]] and [[Mediterranean and Middle East theatre of World War II|Mediterranean and Middle East]] [[List of theaters and campaigns of World War II|theatres]]. The shock of Britain's [[fall of |defeat in ]] in 1942, followed soon after by the [[bombing of Darwin]] and [[Air raids on , 1942–43|other  attacks on  soil]], led to a widespread belief in  that [[Proposed  invasion of  during World War II|a  invasion was imminent]], and a shift from the  to the [[– relations|]] as 's principal ally and security partner. Since 1951,  has been allied with the  under the [[ANZUS]] treaty.

===Post-war and contemporary eras===
{{Main|History of  (1945–present)}}

[[File: Migrant 1954 MariaScholte=50000thToAustraliaPostWW2.jpg|thumb|left|[[Post-war immigration to |Postwar migrants]] from Europe arriving in  in 1954]]
In the three decades following World War II,  experienced significant increases in living standards, leisure time and suburban development. Governments encouraged a [[Post-war immigration to |large wave of immigration from across Europe]] and called these migrants "[[New ]]". High immigration was justified to  using the slogan "populate or perish," and from the 1960s the [[white  policy]] was gradually relaxed.

A member of the [[Western Bloc]] during the [[Cold War]],  participated in the [[ in the  War| War]] and the [[Military history of  during the Malayan Emergency|Malayan Emergency]] during the 1950s and the [[Military history of  during the  War| War]] from 1962 to 1973. Tensions over communist influence in society led to [[1951  Communist Party ban referendum|unsuccessful attempts]] by the [[Menzies Government (1949–1966)|Menzies Government]] to ban the [[Communist Party of ]], and a [[ Labor Party split of 1955|bitter split]] in the [[ Labor Party|Labor Party]] in 1955.

As a result of a [[ referendum, 1967 (Aboriginals)|1967 referendum]], the federal government gained the power to legislate with regard to Aboriginal , and Aboriginal  were fully included in the [[Census in |census]]. [[Aboriginal title|Pre-colonial land interests]] (referred to as [[Native title in |native title]] in ) was recognised in law for the first time when the [[High Court of ]] held in ''[[Mabo v Queensland (No 2)]]'' that  was not ''[[terra nullius]]'' ({{Gloss|land belonging to no one}}) at the time of European settlement.

Following the abolition of the last vestiges of the [[White  policy]] in 1973, 's demography and culture transformed as a result of a large and ongoing wave of non-European immigration, mostly from Asia. The late 20th century also saw an increasing focus on foreign policy ties with other [[Asia–Pacific|Asia{{En dash}}Pacific]] nations. The [[ Acts]] of 1986 severed the remaining constitutional ties between  and the  while maintaining the monarch in her independent capacity as [[Queen of ]]. In a [[1999  republic referendum|1999 constitutional referendum]], 55% of voters rejected [[Republicanism in |abolishing the monarchy]] and becoming a republic.

Following the [[September 11 attacks]] on the ,  joined the  in fighting the [[Military history of  during the War in | War]] from 2001 to 2021 and the [[ contribution to the 2003 invasion of | War]] from 2003 to 2009. The nation's trade relations also became increasingly oriented towards East Asia in the 21st century, with  becoming the nation's [[List of the largest trading partners of |largest trading partner]] by a large margin.

In response to the [[COVID-19 pandemic in |COVID-19 pandemic]], from March 2020 [[COVID-19 lockdowns|lockdowns]] and other restrictions on public gatherings and movement across the national and state borders were implemented by the Federal, state and territory governments. Following the rollout of vaccines in 2021, these restrictions were gradually eased. In October 2023,  declared that COVID-19 was no longer a communicable disease incident of national significance.
== History ==
{{Main|History of |Timeline of  history}}

=== Pre-Columbian<!--This is NOT a typo. Before Christopher Columbus, not before  --> era ===
{{Main|Pre-Columbian cultures of }}
[[File:Culturas precolombinas de .png|thumb|left|Location map of the pre-Columbian cultures of ]]
Owing to its location, the present territory of  was a corridor of early human civilization from [[Mesoamerica]] and the [[Caribbean]] to the [[Andes]] and [[Amazon basin]]. The oldest archaeological finds are from the Pubenza and El Totumo sites in the Magdalena Valley {{convert|100|km|mi|sp=us}} southwest of Bogotá. These sites date from the [[Paleo-|Paleoindian]] period (18,000–8000&nbsp;BCE). At [[Puerto Hormiga archaeological site|Puerto Hormiga]] and other sites, traces from the [[Archaic Period (Americas)|Archaic Period]] (~8000–2000&nbsp;BCE) have been found. Vestiges indicate that there was also early occupation in the regions of [[El Abra]] and [[Tequendama]] in [[Cundinamarca Department|Cundinamarca]]. The oldest pottery discovered in the Americas, found in [[San Jacinto, Bolívar|San Jacinto]], dates to 5000–4000&nbsp;BCE.

Indigenous people inhabited the territory that is now  by 12,500&nbsp;BCE. Nomadic [[hunter-gatherer]] tribes at the El Abra, [[Tibitó]] and Tequendama sites near present-day [[Bogotá]] traded with one another and with other cultures from the [[Magdalena River]] Valley. A site including {{Convert|8|mi|0|spell=in|sp=us}} of [[Pictogram|pictographs]] that is under study at Serranía de la Lindosa was revealed in November 2020. Their age is suggested as being 12,500 years old (c. 10,480 B.C.) by the anthropologists working on the site, because of extinct fauna depicted. It was during the earliest known human occupation of the area.

Between 5000 and 1000&nbsp;BCE, hunter-gatherer tribes transitioned to agrarian societies; fixed settlements were established, and pottery appeared. Beginning in the 1st millennium BCE, groups of [[Indigenous peoples of the Americas|Amerindians]] including the [[Muisca]], [[Zenú]], [[Quimbaya civilization|Quimbaya]], and [[Tairona]] developed the political system of ''[[cacicazgo]]s'' with a pyramidal structure of power headed by ''caciques''. The Muisca inhabited mainly the area of what is now the [[Departments of |Departments]] of [[Boyacá Department|Boyacá]] and [[Cundinamarca Department|Cundinamarca]] high plateau (''[[Altiplano Cundiboyacense]]'') where they formed the [[Muisca Confederation]]. They farmed maize, potato, quinoa, and cotton, and traded gold, [[ emeralds|emeralds]], blankets, ceramic handicrafts, coca and especially [[Halite|rock salt]] with neighboring nations. The Tairona inhabited northern  in the isolated mountain range of [[Sierra Nevada de Santa Marta]]. The Quimbaya inhabited regions of the [[Cauca River]] Valley between the [[Cordillera Occidental ()|Western]] and [[Cordillera Central ()|Central]] Ranges of the  Andes. Most of the Amerindians practiced agriculture and the social structure of each indigenous community was different. Some groups of indigenous people such as the Caribs lived in a state of permanent war, but others had less bellicose attitudes. During the 1200s, [[Austronesian expansion|Malayo-Polynesian]]s and [[Indigenous peoples in |Native ]] in  made contact, thereby spreading Native  genetics from Precolonial  to some Pacific Ocean islands.

=== Colonial period ===
{{Main|New Kingdom of Granada|Viceroyalty of New Granada}}
{{See also| conquest of New Granada| conquest of the Muisca| colonization of the Americas| Empire}}
[[File:Retrato_de_Vasco_Nuñez_de_Balboa_(1475-1517)_-_Anónimo.jpg|upright|thumb|[[Vasco Núñez de Balboa]], founder of [[Santa María la Antigua del Darién]], the first stable European settlement on the continent]]

[[Alonso de Ojeda]] (who had sailed with Columbus) reached the [[Guajira Peninsula]] in 1499.  explorers, led by [[Rodrigo de Bastidas]], made the first exploration of the [[Caribbean Basin|Caribbean coast]] in 1500. [[Christopher Columbus]] navigated near the Caribbean in 1502. In 1508, [[Vasco Núñez de Balboa]] accompanied an expedition to the territory through the region of [[Gulf of Urabá]] and they founded the town of [[Santa María la Antigua del Darién]] in 1510, the first stable settlement on the continent.{{efn|Balboa is best known for being the first European to see the Pacific Ocean in 1513, which he called ''Mar del Sur'' (or "Sea of the South") and would facilitate  exploration and settlement of South America.}} [[Santa Marta]] was founded in 1525, and [[Cartagena, |Cartagena]] in 1533.  [[conquistador]] [[Gonzalo Jiménez de Quesada]] led an expedition to the interior in April 1536, and christened the districts through which he passed "[[New Kingdom of Granada]]". In August 1538, he provisionally founded its capital near the Muisca [[cacicazgo]] of [[Bacatá|Muyquytá]], and named it "Santa Fe". The name soon acquired a suffix and was called Santa Fe de Bogotá. Two other notable journeys by early conquistadors to the interior took place in the same period. [[Sebastián de Belalcázar]], conqueror of [[Quito]], traveled north and founded [[Cali]], in 1536, and [[Popayán]], in 1537; from 1536 to 1539,  conquistador [[Nikolaus Federmann]] crossed the [[Orinoquía natural region|Llanos Orientales]] and went over the [[Cordillera Oriental ()|Cordillera Oriental]] in a search for [[El Dorado]], the "city of gold". The legend and the gold would play a pivotal role in luring the  and other Europeans to New Granada during the 16th and 17th centuries.

The [[List of conquistadors in |conquistadors]] made frequent alliances with the enemies of different indigenous communities. [[ auxiliaries|Indigenous allies]] were crucial to conquest, as well as to creating and maintaining empire. Indigenous peoples in  experienced a decline in population due to conquest as well as Eurasian diseases, such as [[smallpox]], to which they had no immunity. Regarding the land as deserted, the  Crown sold properties to all persons interested in colonized territories, creating large farms and possession of mines. In the 16th century, the [[Navigation|nautical science]] in  reached a great development thanks to numerous scientific figures of the [[Casa de Contratación]] and nautical science was an essential pillar of the [[Iberian ship development, 1400–1600|Iberian expansion]]. In 1542, the region of New Granada, along with all other  possessions in South America, became part of the [[Viceroyalty of ]], with its capital in [[Lima]]. In 1547, New Granada became a separate captaincy-general within the viceroyalty, with its capital at Santa Fe de Bogota. In 1549, the [[Real Audiencia|Royal Audiencia]] was created by a royal decree, and New Granada was ruled by the [[Royal Audience of Santa Fe de Bogotá]], which at that time comprised the provinces of Santa Marta, Rio de San Juan, Popayán, Guayana and Cartagena. But important decisions were taken from the colony to  by the [[Council of the Indies]].
