=== <span class="anchor" id="Independence"></span> Independence ===
 declared its [[sovereignty]] within the Soviet Union on 25 October 1990. Following the failed August 1991 [[1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt|coup attempt]] in Moscow, the country proclaimed full independence on 16 December 1991, becoming the last Soviet republic to do so. Ten days after 's declaration, the Soviet Union itself dissolved. This period marked a significant turning point in 's history, as it embarked on a new political and economic path separate from Moscow's control.

[[Nursultan Nazarbayev]], the communist-era leader of , became the country's first president. Under his leadership,  transitioned from a Soviet-era planned economy to a market economy, focusing on privatization and foreign investments. The emphasis on economic reform, particularly in the oil sector, helped  become one of Central Asia's most economically powerful nations. By 2006,  contributed around 60% of the region's GDP, primarily through its oil exports. However, political reforms lagged behind these economic strides, and Nazarbayev maintained an authoritarian rule throughout his presidency.

In 1997, Nazarbayev [[Capital relocation in |moved the capital]] from Almaty, the country's largest city, to [[Astana]] (later renamed Nur-Sultan in 2019), a decision that symbolized the government's desire to modernize and assert control over the country's vast territories. The capital city change was part of broader efforts to establish a new national identity and shift the political center from former Soviet-era heartlands.

's political landscape during Nazarbayev's rule was characterized by limited political pluralism. In the 2004 parliamentary elections, the pro-government Otan Party, led by Nazarbayev, dominated the Majilis (the lower house of parliament). Other parties sympathetic to the president, such as the agrarian-industrial bloc AIST and the Asar party (founded by Nazarbayev's daughter), secured most of the remaining seats, while opposition parties struggled to gain representation. International observers, including the Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe, criticized the elections for not meeting democratic standards.

Despite claims of progress toward democracy, 's political system remained authoritarian well into the 21st century. In 2010, the country was still ranked as an [[Authoritarianism|authoritarian regime]] on ''[[The Economist]]'''s [[The Economist Democracy Index|Democracy Index]]. Nazarbayev, who had ruled since independence, announced his resignation on 19 March 2019, after nearly three decades in power. His successor, [[Kassym-Jomart Tokayev]], won the 2019 presidential election and took office on 12 June 2019. Tokayev's first official act was to rename the capital city to Nur-Sultan, in honor of Nazarbayev's legacy.

However, Tokayev's presidency faced significant challenges. In January 2022,  was gripped by [[2022  unrest|large-scale protests]] following a sharp rise in fuel prices. The unrest quickly escalated, and Tokayev responded decisively by assuming control of the country's Security Council, removing Nazarbayev from the post and consolidating his own power. This marked a dramatic shift in 's political dynamics, with Tokayev signaling a departure from the old Nazarbayev-era system. In September 2022, the capital's name was reverted back to Astana, a move seen as part of the broader efforts to distance the country from the former president's influence.
== History ==
{{Main|History of }}
[[File:Stone spheres of . Museo Nacional.jpg|thumb|[[Stone spheres of |Stone spheres]] created by the [[Diquis]] culture at the [[Museo Nacional de |National Museum of ]]. [[Stone spheres of |The sphere]] is the icon of the country's cultural identity.]]

=== Pre-Columbian period ===
{{Main|Pre-Columbian history of }}
Historians have classified the [[Indigenous peoples of the Americas|Indigenous people]] of  as belonging to the [[Intermediate Area]], where the peripheries of the [[Mesoamerican]] and [[Andean world|Andean]] native cultures overlapped. More recently, [[Pre-Columbian era|pre-Columbian]]  has also been described as part of the [[Isthmo- Area]].

Stone tools, the oldest evidence of human occupation in , are associated with the arrival of various groups of [[hunter-gatherer]]s about 10,000 to 7,000 years [[Before Common Era|BCE]] in the [[Turrialba (district)|Turrialba Valley]]. The presence of [[Clovis culture]] type spearheads and arrows from [[South America]] opens the possibility that, in this area, two different cultures coexisted.

Agriculture became evident in the populations that lived in  about 5,000 years ago. They mainly grew [[tubers]] and roots. For the first and second millennia BCE there were already settled farming communities. These were small and scattered, although the timing of the transition from [[hunter-gatherer|hunting]] and gathering to agriculture as the main livelihood in the territory is still unknown.

The earliest use of [[pottery]] appears around 2,000 to 3,000 BCE. Shards of pots, cylindrical vases, platters, gourds, and other vases decorated with grooves, prints, and some modeled after animals have been found.

The influence of Indigenous peoples on modern  culture has been relatively small compared to other nations since the country lacked a strong native civilization to begin with.{{clarify|date=October 2024}}{{citation needed|date=October 2024}} Most of the native population was absorbed into the -speaking [[ colonization of the Americas|colonial society]] through inter-marriage,{{citation needed|date=October 2024}} except for some small remnants, the most significant of which are the [[Bribri people|Bribri]] and [[Boruca people|Boruca]] tribes who still inhabit the mountains of the [[Cordillera de Talamanca]], in the southeastern part of , near the frontier with [[]].

===  colonization ===
The name {{lang|es|la }}, meaning "rich coast" in the  language, was in some accounts first applied by [[Christopher Columbus]], who sailed to the eastern shores of  during his final voyage in 1502, and reported vast quantities of gold jewelry worn by natives. The name may also have come from conquistador [[Gil González Dávila]], who landed on the west coast in 1522, encountered natives, and obtained some of their gold, sometimes by violent theft and sometimes as gifts from local leaders.

[[File:Iglesia Inmaculada Concepcion Ujarras.jpg|thumb|The {{lang|es|[[Ujarrás]]|italic=no}} historical site in the Orosí Valley, [[Cartago province]]. The church was built between 1686 and 1693.]]
During most of the colonial period,  was the southernmost province of the [[Captaincy General of ]], nominally part of the [[New |Viceroyalty of New ]]. The captaincy general was a largely autonomous entity within the [[ Empire]]. 's distance from the capital of the captaincy in [[]], its legal prohibition under [[mercantilism|mercantilist]]  law from trade with its southern neighbor , then part of the [[Viceroyalty of New Granada]] (i.e. [[]]), and lack of resources such as gold and silver, made  into a poor, isolated, and sparsely inhabited region within the  Empire.  was described as "the poorest and most miserable  colony in all America" by a  governor in 1719.

=== Independence ===
{{See also|Free State of |First  Republic}}
Like the rest of [[Central America]],  never fought for independence from . On 15 September 1821, after the final  defeat in the [[ War of Independence]] (1810–1821), the authorities in  declared the independence of all of Central America. That date is still celebrated as Independence Day in  even though, technically, under the [[ Constitution of 1812]] that had been readopted in 1820, [[]] and  had become an autonomous province with its capital in [[León, |León]].

On 3 March 1824, the government of the State of  officially proposed to the municipality of [[Nicoya]] its voluntary incorporation into the country, through a document in which it invited it "if it was convenient to join its Province without going against its will." On 4 July, an open town hall was convened in Nicoya to discuss the matter, but attendees declined the invitation under the argument "that this Party... cannot be dissident."

On 25 July 1824, a second [[plebiscite]] was called in the city of Nicoya. After deliberation, the incorporation into  was decided in an open town hall meeting, preparing a record in which the main reasons for it were noted, pointing out the advantages in terms of trade, the desire to participate in the advances that are palpable in , the economic, administrative and public service benefits, the creation of schools, security and quiet, referring to the state of war that  was experiencing at that time and the fear that it would spread to the Partido populations, in addition to point out the poverty in which its towns find themselves and the geography of the territory as justifications for the union. Three days later, another similar plebiscite was held in [[Santa Cruz (canton), |Santa Cruz]], with the same result. The election was by majority vote, with 77% of the Party's population in favor of incorporation, and 23% against it. The town of Guanacaste was the only one that declined annexation, due to the ties its residents had with the city of [[Rivas, ]].

Upon independence,  authorities faced the issue of officially deciding the future of the country. Two bands formed: the Imperialists, defended by [[Cartago, |Cartago]] and [[Heredia Province|Heredia cities]], which were in favor of [[Central America under  rule|joining]] the [[First  Empire| Empire]], and the Republicans, represented by the cities of [[San José, |San José]] and [[Alajuela]] who defended full independence. Because of the lack of agreement on these two possible outcomes, the first civil war in  occurred. The [[Battle of Ochomogo]] took place on the Hill of [[Ochomogo]], located in the [[ Central Valley|Central Valley]] in 1823. The conflict was won by the Republicans and, as a consequence, the city of [[Cartago, |Cartago]] lost its status as the capital, which moved to [[San José, |San José]].
[[File:First postal stamp CR 4 Reales 1863.jpg|thumb|upright|1849 [[Coat of arms of |national coat of arms]] was featured in the first postal stamp issued in 1862.]]

In 1838, long after the [[Federal Republic of Central America]] ceased to function in practice,  formally withdrew and proclaimed itself sovereign. The considerable distance and poor communication routes between [[ City]] and the Central Plateau, where most of the  population lived then and still lives now, meant the local population had little allegiance to the federal government in . Since colonial times,  has been reluctant to become economically tied with the rest of Central America. Even today, despite most of its neighbors'{{Efn|, , , , and }} efforts to increase regional integration,  has remained more independent.

Until 1849, when it became part of [[]], [[Chiriquí province|Chiriquí]] was part of .  pride was assuaged for the loss of this eastern (or southern) territory with the acquisition of [[Guanacaste Province|Guanacaste]], in the north.

=== Economic growth in the 19th century ===
{{See also|Liberal State}}
[[Coffee]] was first planted in  in 1808, and by the 1820s, it surpassed [[tobacco]], [[sugar]], and [[cacao bean|cacao]] as a primary [[export]]. Coffee production remained 's principal source of wealth well into the 20th century, creating a wealthy class of growers, the so-called Coffee Barons. The revenue helped to modernize the country.

Most of the coffee exported was grown around the main centers of population in the Central Plateau and then transported by [[Bullock cart|oxcart]] to the [[Pacific Ocean|Pacific]] port of [[Puntarenas]] after the main road was built in 1846. By the mid-1850s the main market for coffee was Britain. It soon became a high priority to develop an effective transportation route from the Central Plateau to the Atlantic Ocean. For this purpose, in the 1870s, the  government contracted with U.S. businessman [[Minor C. Keith]] to build a railroad from San José to the [[Western Caribbean Zone|Caribbean]] port of [[Limón]]. Despite enormous difficulties with construction, disease, and financing, the railroad was completed in 1890.

Most Afro- descend from [[]]n immigrants who worked in the construction of that railway and now make up about 3% of 's population.{{Citation needed|date=February 2022}} U.S. convicts, , and  immigrants also participated in the construction project. In exchange for completing the railroad, the  government granted Keith large tracts of land and a lease on the train route, which he used to produce [[banana]]s and export them to the . As a result, bananas came to rival coffee as the principal  export, while foreign-owned corporations (including the [[United Fruit Company]] later) began to hold a major role in the national economy and eventually became a symbol of the exploitative export economy. The major labor dispute between the peasants and the United Fruit Company (The Great Banana Strike) was a major event in the country's history and was an important step that would eventually lead to the formation of effective [[trade unions in ]], as the company was required to sign a collective agreement with its workers in 1938.

=== 20th century ===
{{See also|Reform State}}
Historically,  has generally enjoyed greater peace and more consistent political stability than many of its fellow Latin  nations. During the 20th century, however,  experienced two significant periods of violence. In 1917–1919, General [[Federico Tinoco Granados]] ruled as a military dictator until he was overthrown and forced into exile. The unpopularity of [[Dictatorship of the Tinoco Brothers|Tinoco's regime]] led, after he was overthrown, to a considerable decline in the size, wealth, and political influence of the  military. In 1948, [[José Figueres Ferrer]] led an [[ Civil War|armed uprising]] in the wake of a disputed presidential election between [[Rafael Ángel Calderón Guardia]] (who had been president between 1940 and 1944) and [[Otilio Ulate Blanco]]. With more than 2,000 dead, the resulting 44-day [[ Civil War]] was the bloodiest event in  during the 20th century.

The victorious rebels formed a government junta that [[military of |abolished the military]] all together and oversaw the drafting of a new constitution by a democratically elected assembly. Having enacted these reforms, the junta transferred power to Ulate on 8 November 1949. After the ''coup d'état'', Figueres became a national hero, winning the country's first democratic election under the new constitution [[ general election, 1953|in 1953]]. Since then,  has held 15 additional presidential elections, the latest [[ general election, 2022|in 2022]]. With uninterrupted democracy dating back to at least 1948, the country is the region's most stable.
== History ==
{{Main|History of the }}

=== Antiquity ===
[[File:Cántaro (26738115330).jpg|thumb|left|upright|2nd century [[Common Era|BCE]] era jar found in [[Mleiha Archaeological Centre|Mleiha Archaeological site]] in Sharjah]]

Stone tools recovered reveal a settlement of people from Africa some 127,000 years ago and a stone tool used for butchering animals discovered on the Arabian coast suggests an even older habitation from 130,000 years ago. In time, lively trading links developed with civilisations in [[Mesopotamia]], , and the [[Indus Valley civilisation|Harappan culture]] of the Indus Valley. This contact persisted and became wider, probably motivated by the trade in copper from the [[Hajar Mountains]], which commenced around 3,000 BCE. Sumerian sources talk of the [[Magan (civilization)|Magan]] civilisation, which has been identified as encompassing the modern UAE and .

There are six periods of human settlement with distinctive behaviours in the region before Islam, which include the [[Hafit period]] from 3,200 to 2,600 BCE, the [[Umm Al Nar culture]] from 2,600 to 2,000 BCE, and the [[Wadi Suq culture]] from 2,000 to 1,300 BCE. From 1,200 BCE to the advent of Islam in Eastern Arabia, through three distinctive [[Iron Age in the |Iron Ages]] and the [[Mleiha]] period, the area was variously occupied by the [[Achaemenid Empire|Achaemenids]] and other forces, and saw the construction of fortified settlements and extensive husbandry thanks to the development of the [[Qanat|''falaj'']] irrigation system.

===Islam===
The spread of [[Islam]] to the northeastern tip of the [[Arabian Peninsula]] is thought to have followed directly from a letter sent by the [[Islamic prophet]] [[Muhammad]] to the rulers of [[]] in 630 CE. This led to a group of rulers travelling to [[Medina]], converting to Islam, and subsequently driving a successful uprising against the unpopular [[Sasanian Empire|Sassanids]], who dominated the coast at the time.{{sfnp|Heard-Bey|1996|p=127}} Following the death of Muhammad, the new Islamic communities south of the [[Persian Gulf]] threatened to disintegrate, with insurrections against the [[Muslim leaders]]. Caliph [[Abu Bakr]] sent an army from the capital [[Medina]] which completed its reconquest of the territory ([[Ridda wars|the Ridda Wars]]) with the [[Battle of Dibba]] in which 10,000 lives are thought to have been lost.{{sfnp|Heard-Bey|1996|pp=127–128}} This assured the integrity of the [[Caliphate]] and the unification of the Arabian Peninsula under the newly emerging [[Rashidun Caliphate]].

In 637, Julfar (in the area of today's [[Ras Al Khaimah]]) was an important port that was used as a staging post for the Islamic invasion of the [[Sasanian Empire]]. The area of the [[Al Ain]]/[[Buraimi Oasis]] was known as Tu'am and was an important trading post for camel routes between the coast and the Arabian interior.{{sfnp|Heard-Bey|1996|pp=22–23}}

The earliest [[Christianity|Christian]] site in the UAE was first discovered in the 1990s, an extensive monastic complex on what is now known as [[Sir Bani Yas]] Island and which dates back to the seventh century. Thought to be [[Nestorianism|Nestorian]] and built in 600 CE, the church appears to have been abandoned peacefully in 750 CE. It forms a rare physical link to a legacy of Christianity, which is thought to have spread across the peninsula from 50 to 350 CE following trade routes. Certainly, by the fifth century,  had a bishop named John – the last bishop of  being Etienne, in 676 CE.

===  era ===
{{See also|Battle of the Strait of Hormuz (1553)|Piracy in the Persian Gulf}}
[[File:Forte de doba.jpg|thumb|left|A painting of the [[ Empire]] {{ill|Doba Fortress|pt|Forte de Doba|vertical-align=sup}} in [[Dibba Al-Hisn]] in 1620]]

The harsh desert environment led to the emergence of the "versatile tribesman", nomadic groups who subsisted due to a variety of economic activities, including animal husbandry, agriculture, and hunting. The seasonal movements of these groups led not only to frequent clashes between groups but also to the establishment of seasonal and semi-seasonal settlements and centres. These formed tribal groupings whose names are still carried by modern , including the [[Bani Yas]] and [[Al Nahyan family|Al Bu Falah]] of [[Abu Dhabi]], Al Ain, [[Liwa Oasis|Liwa]], and the west coast; the [[Dhawahir]], Awamir, [[Al Ali (tribe)|Al Ali]], and [[Manasir (tribe)|Manasir]] of the interior; the [[Sharqiyin]] of the east coast; and the [[Al-Qasimi|Qawasim]] to the north.

With the expansion of European [[colonial empire]]s, [[ Empire|]], [[ Empire|]], and [[ Empire|]] forces appeared in the Persian Gulf region. By the 18th century, the Bani Yas confederation was the dominant force in most of the area now known as Abu Dhabi,{{sfnp|Heard-Bey|1996|p=43}} while the Northern [[Al-Qasimi|Al Qawasim]] (Al Qasimi) dominated maritime commerce. The  maintained an influence over the coastal settlements, building [[Fortification|forts]] in the wake of the bloody 16th-century conquests of coastal communities by [[Afonso de Albuquerque|Albuquerque]] and the  commanders who followed him – particularly on the east coast at [[Muscat]], [[Sohar]], and [[Khor Fakkan]].{{sfnp|Heard-Bey|1996|p=282}}

The southern coast of the Persian Gulf was known to the  as the "[[History of the |Pirate Coast]]", as boats of the Al Qawasim federation harassed -flagged shipping from the 17th century into the 19th. The charge of piracy is disputed by modern  historians, including the current ruler of Sharjah, [[Sultan bin Muhammad Al-Qasimi|Sheikh Sultan Al Qasimi]], in his 1986 book ''The Myth of Arab Piracy in the Gulf''.
[[File:Persian Gulf 1507-1750.gif|alt=|thumb|Purple – [[ Empire|]] in the Persian Gulf in the 16th and 17th century. Main cities, ports, and routes.]]
[[File:Ras Al Khaimah under attack, 1809 01.jpg|thumb|A painting depicting the burning of the coastal town and port of [[Emirate of Ras Al Khaimah]] during the [[Persian Gulf campaign of 1809]]]]

 expeditions to protect their  trade routes led to campaigns against Ras Al Khaimah and other harbours along the coast, including the [[Persian Gulf campaign of 1809]] and the more successful [[Persian Gulf campaign of 1819|campaign of 1819]]. The following year, Britain and a number of local rulers signed a [[General Maritime Treaty of 1820|maritime truce]], giving rise to the term [[Trucial States]], which came to define the status of the coastal emirates. A further treaty was signed in 1843 and in 1853, the [[Perpetual Maritime Truce]] was agreed. To this was added the 'Exclusive Agreements', signed in 1892, which made the [[Trucial States]] a  protectorate.

Under the 1892 treaty, the trucial sheikhs agreed not to dispose of any territory except to the  and not to enter into relationships with any foreign government other than the  without their consent. In return, the  promised to protect the Trucial Coast from all aggression by sea and to help in case of land attack.  maritime policing meant that pearling fleets could operate in relative security. However, the  prohibition of the [[History of slavery|slave trade]] meant an important source of income was lost to some sheikhs and merchants.

In 1869, the Qubaisat tribe settled at [[Khor Al Adaid]] and tried to enlist the support of the Ottomans. Khor Al Adaid was claimed by Abu Dhabi at that time, a claim supported by the . In 1906, the  Political Resident, [[Percy Cox]], confirmed in writing to the ruler of Abu Dhabi, [[Zayed bin Khalifa Al Nahyan]] ('Zayed the Great'), that Khor Al Adaid belonged to his sheikhdom.

===  era and discovery of oil ===
{{See also|Persian Gulf campaign of 1809|Persian Gulf campaign of 1819|General Maritime Treaty of 1820|Trucial States}}
[[File:Dhayah Fort showing hilltop location.jpg|thumb|[[Dhayah Fort]] at the hill top. In 1819 it was the last [[Al-Qasimi]] stronghold to fall in the [[Persian Gulf campaign of 1819]]. The fall of Dhayah was to pave the way for the signing of the [[General Maritime Treaty of 1820]].]]

During the 19th and early 20th centuries, the [[Pearl hunting|pearling industry]] thrived, providing both income and employment to the people of the Persian Gulf. The [[World War I|First World War]] had a severe impact on the industry, but it was the [[economic depression]] of the late 1920s and early 1930s, coupled with the invention of the [[cultured pearl]], that wiped out the trade. The remnants of the trade eventually faded away shortly after the [[World War II|Second World War]], when the newly independent [[Government of ]] imposed heavy taxation on imported pearls. The decline of pearling resulted in extreme economic hardship in the Trucial States.

In 1922, the  government secured undertakings from the rulers of the Trucial States not to sign concessions with foreign companies without their consent. Aware of the potential for the development of natural resources such as oil, following finds in Persia (from 1908) and Mesopotamia (from 1927), a -led oil company, the [[ Petroleum Company]] (IPC), showed an interest in the region. The [[Anglo-Persian Oil Company]] (APOC, later to become [[BP| Petroleum]], or BP) had a 23.75% share in IPC. From 1935, onshore concessions to explore for oil were granted by local rulers, with APOC signing the first one on behalf of Petroleum Concessions Ltd (PCL), an associate company of IPC. APOC was prevented from developing the region alone because of the restrictions of the [[Red Line Agreement]], which required it to operate through IPC. A number of options between PCL and the trucial rulers were signed, providing useful revenue for communities experiencing poverty following the collapse of the pearl trade. However, the wealth of oil which the rulers could see from the revenues accruing to surrounding countries remained elusive. The first bore holes in Abu Dhabi were drilled by IPC's operating company, Petroleum Development (Trucial Coast) Ltd (PDTC) at Ras Sadr in 1950, with a {{convert|13000|ft|m|abbr=off|adj=mid|-deep}} bore hole taking a year to drill and turning out dry, at the tremendous cost at the time of £1 million.

[[File:Mid-20th century Dubai.JPG|thumb|left|Dubai in 1950: the area in this photo shows [[Bur Dubai]] in the foreground (centred on [[Al-Fahidi Fort]]), [[Deira, Dubai|Deira]] in middle-right on the other side of the creek, and [[Al Shindagha]] (left) and [[Al Ras, Dubai|Al Ras]] (right) in the background across the creek, from Deira.]]
The  set up a development office that helped in some small developments in the emirates. The seven [[sheikh]]s of the [[Emirates of the |emirates]] then decided to form a council to coordinate matters between them and took over the development office. In 1952, they formed the Trucial States Council, and appointed [[Adi Bitar|Adi Al Bitar]], Dubai's [[Rashid bin Saeed Al Maktoum|Sheikh Rashid bin Saeed Al Maktoum]]'s legal advisor, as secretary general and legal advisor to the council. The council was terminated once the  was formed. The tribal nature of society and the lack of definition of borders between emirates frequently led to disputes, settled either through mediation or, more rarely, force. The [[Trucial  Scouts]] was a small military force used by the  to keep the peace.

In 1953, a subsidiary of [[BP]], D'Arcy Exploration Ltd, obtained an offshore concession from the ruler of Abu Dhabi. BP joined with [[Total SE|Compagnie Française des Pétroles]] (later [[Total SE|Total]]) to form operating companies, Abu Dhabi Marine Areas Ltd (ADMA) and Dubai Marine Areas Ltd (DUMA). A number of undersea oil surveys were carried out, including one led by the famous marine explorer [[Jacques Cousteau]]. In 1958, a floating platform rig was towed from [[Hamburg]], [[]], and positioned over the [[Umm Shaif oil field|Umm Shaif]] pearl bed, in Abu Dhabi waters, where drilling began. In March, it struck oil in the Upper Thamama rock formation. This was the first commercial discovery of the Trucial Coast, leading to the first exports of oil in 1962. ADMA made further offshore discoveries at Zakum and elsewhere, and other companies made commercial finds such as the [[Fateh Oil Field|Fateh oilfield]] off Dubai and the Mubarak field off Sharjah (shared with ).

Meanwhile, onshore exploration was hindered by territorial disputes. In 1955, the [[]] represented Abu Dhabi and  in their dispute with  over the [[Al Buraimi Governorate|Buraimi Oasis]]. A 1974 agreement between Abu Dhabi and  seemed to have settled the Abu Dhabi- [[Territorial dispute|border dispute]], but this has not been ratified. The UAE's border with  was ratified in 2008.

PDTC continued its onshore exploration away from the disputed area, drilling five more bore holes that were also dry. However, on 27 October 1960, the company discovered oil in commercial quantities at the Murban No. 3 well on the coast near Tarif. In 1962, PDTC became the [[Abu Dhabi Petroleum Company]]. As oil revenues increased, the ruler of Abu Dhabi, [[Zayed bin Sultan Al Nahyan]], undertook a massive construction program, building schools, housing, hospitals, and roads. When Dubai's oil exports commenced in 1969, Sheikh [[Rashid bin Saeed Al Maktoum]], the ruler of Dubai, was able to invest the revenues from the limited reserves found to spark the diversification drive that would create the modern [[global city]] of Dubai.

=== Independence ===
{{See also|Foundation of the |Seizure of Abu Musa and the Greater and Lesser Tunbs}}
[[File:Flag-hoisting at the Union Declaration.jpg|thumb|left|Historic photo depicting the first hoisting of the  flag by the rulers of the emirates at the Union House in Dubai on 2 December 1971]]

By 1966, it had become clear that the  government could no longer afford to administer and protect the [[Trucial States]], what is now the .  [[Member of Parliament ()|Members of Parliament]] (MPs) debated the preparedness of the [[Royal Navy]] to defend the [[sheikhdom]]s. On 24 January 1968,  Prime Minister [[Harold Wilson]] announced the government's decision, reaffirmed in March 1971 by Prime Minister [[Edward Heath]], to end the treaty relationships with the seven trucial sheikhdoms. Days after the announcement, the ruler of Abu Dhabi, Sheikh [[Zayed bin Sultan Al Nahyan]], fearing vulnerability, tried to persuade the  to honour the protection treaties by offering to pay the full costs of keeping the [[ Armed Forces]] in the Emirates. The  [[Conservative Party (UK)|Conservative]] government rejected the offer. After [[Labour Party (UK)|Labour]] MP [[Goronwy Roberts, Baron Goronwy-Roberts|Goronwy Roberts]] informed Sheikh Zayed of the news of  withdrawal, the nine Persian Gulf sheikhdoms attempted to form a union of Arab emirates, but by mid-1971 they were still unable to agree on terms of union even though the  treaty relationship was to expire in December of that year.

Fears of vulnerability were realised the day before independence. An  destroyer group broke formation from an exercise in the lower Gulf, sailing to the [[Greater and Lesser Tunbs|Tunb islands]]. The islands were [[Seizure of Abu Musa and the Greater and Lesser Tunbs|taken by force]], civilians and Arab defenders alike allowed to flee. A  warship stood idle during the course of the invasion. A destroyer group approached the island of [[Abu Musa]] as well. But there, [[Khalid bin Muhammad Al Qasimi|Sheikh Khalid bin Muhammad Al Qasimi]] had already negotiated with the  shah, and the island was quickly leased to  for $3 million a year. Meanwhile,  laid claim to swathes of Abu Dhabi. It was not until 1974 that a [[Treaty of Jeddah (1974)|border agreement]] was signed with , formally demarcating the frontiers between the UAE and . The UAE's sense of threat from  influenced its financial support for [[Ba'athist |]] during the [[– War]].

Originally intended to be part of the proposed Federation of Arab Emirates,  became independent in August, and  in September 1971. When the -Trucial Sheikhdoms treaty expired on 1 December 1971, both emirates became fully independent. On 2 December 1971, six of the emirates (Abu Dhabi, Ajman, Dubai, Fujairah, Sharjah, and Umm Al Quwain) agreed to enter into a union named the . [[Emirate of Ras Al Khaimah|Ras al-Khaimah]] joined later, on 10 January 1972. In February 1972, the [[Federal National Council]] (FNC) was created; it was a 40-member consultative body appointed by the seven rulers. The UAE joined the [[Arab League]] on 6 December 1971 and the [[United Nations]] on 9 December. It was a founding member of the [[Gulf Cooperation Council]] in May 1981, with Abu Dhabi hosting the first [[GCC Summit|GCC summit]].

=== Post-independence period ===
{{Expand section|date=November 2025}}
The founding fathers of the  were: [[Zayed bin Sultan Al Nahyan]] of [[Abu Dhabi]]; [[Rashid bin Saeed Al Maktoum]] of [[Dubai]]; [[Khalid bin Muhammad Al Qasimi]] of [[Sharjah]]; [[Rashid bin Humaid Al Nuaimi III|Rashid bin Humaid Al Nuaimi]] of [[Ajman]]; [[Ahmad bin Rashid Al Mualla]] of [[Umm Al Quwain]]; [[Saqr bin Mohammed Al Qasimi]] of [[Ras Al Khaimah]] and [[Mohammed bin Hamad Al Sharqi]] of [[Fujairah]].[[File:Burj Khalifa (worlds tallest building) and the Dubai skyline (25781049892).jpg|thumb|Skyline of [[Dubai]]]]
The UAE supported military operations by the US and other [[Coalition of the Gulf War|coalition states]] engaged in the [[Gulf War]] against [[Saddam Hussein]] in [[Ba'athist ]] (1991), as well as operations supporting the global [[war on terror]] for the [[Horn of Africa]] at [[Al Dhafra Air Base]] located outside of Abu Dhabi. The air base also supported Allied operations during the 1991 Persian [[Gulf War]] and [[Operation Northern Watch]]. The country had already signed a [[military]] defence agreement with the U.S. in 1994 and one with  in 1995. In January 2008,  and the UAE signed a deal allowing  to set up a permanent military base in the emirate of Abu Dhabi. The UAE joined international military operations in  in March 2011.

On 2 November 2004, the UAE's first president, Sheikh [[Zayed bin Sultan Al Nahyan]], died. Sheikh [[Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan]] was elected as the [[President of the |president of the UAE]]. Sheikh [[Mohammed bin Zayed Al Nahyan]] succeeded Sheikh Khalifa as crown prince of Abu Dhabi. In January 2006, Sheikh [[Maktoum bin Rashid Al Maktoum]], the prime minister of the UAE and the ruler of Dubai, died, and Sheikh [[Mohammed bin Rashid Al Maktoum]] assumed both roles.

The first ever national elections were held on 16 December 2006. A number of voters chose half of the members of the [[Federal National Council]]. The UAE has largely escaped the [[Arab Spring]], which other countries have experienced; however, 60  activists from [[Al Islah ()|Al Islah]] were apprehended for an alleged coup attempt and the attempt of the establishment of an [[Islamism|Islamist]] state in the UAE. Mindful of the protests in nearby , in November 2012 the UAE outlawed online mockery of its government or attempts to organise public protests through social media.

On 29 January 2020, the [[COVID-19 pandemic]] was confirmed to have [[COVID-19 pandemic in the |reached the UAE]]. Two months later, in March, the government announced the closure of shopping malls, schools, and places of worship, in addition to imposing a 24-hour curfew, and suspending all [[Emirates (airline)|Emirates]] passenger flights. This resulted in a major economic downturn, which eventually led to the merger of more than 50% of the UAE's [[:Category: federal entities|federal agencies]].

On 29 August 2020, the UAE established normal diplomatic relations with [[]] and with the help of the [[]], they signed the [[Abraham Accords]] with [[]].

On 9 February 2021, the UAE achieved a historic milestone when its probe, named ''[[Emirates Mars Mission|Hope]]'', successfully reached [[Mars]]'s orbit. The UAE became the first country in the [[Arab world]] to reach Mars, the fifth country to successfully reach Mars, and the second country, after an [[Mars Orbiter Mission| probe]], to orbit Mars on its maiden attempt.

On 14 May 2022, Sheikh [[Mohamed bin Zayed Al Nahyan]] was elected as the UAE's new president after the death of [[Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan|Sheikh Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan]].
==History==
{{Main|History of }}
{{Further|Timeline of  history|Historiography of }}

===Indigenous peoples===
The [[Settlement of the Americas|first inhabitants of North America]] are generally hypothesized to have migrated from [[Siberia]] by way of the [[Beringia|Bering land bridge]] and arrived at least 14,000 years ago. The [[Paleo-]] archeological sites at [[Old Crow Flats]] and [[Bluefish Caves]] are two of the oldest sites of human habitation in . The [[Technological and industrial history of #The Stone Age: Fire (14,000 BC – AD 1600)|characteristics of Indigenous societies]] included permanent settlements, agriculture, complex societal hierarchies, and trading networks. Some of these cultures had collapsed by the time European explorers arrived in the late 15th and early 16th centuries and have only been discovered through archeological investigations. [[Indigenous peoples in |Indigenous peoples in present-day ]] include the [[First Nations in |First Nations]], [[Inuit]], and [[Métis people in |Métis]], the last being of [[mixed-blood|mixed descent]] who originated in the mid-17th century when First Nations people married European settlers and their offspring subsequently developed their own identity.[[File:Indigenous population by census division.svg|upright=1.3|thumb|A map of  showing the percent of [[Population of #Indigenous peoples|self-reported indigenous identity]] (First Nations, Inuit, Métis) by census division, according to the [[2021  census]]]]

The [[Population history of indigenous peoples of the Americas|Indigenous population]] at the time of the first European settlements is estimated to have been between 200,000 and two million, with a figure of 500,000 accepted by 's [[Royal Commission on Aboriginal Peoples]]. As a consequence of European colonization, the Indigenous population declined by forty to eighty percent. The decline is attributed to several causes, including the [[Columbian exchange|transfer of European diseases]], to which they had no natural immunity, conflicts over the fur trade, conflicts with the colonial authorities and settlers, and the loss of Indigenous lands to settlers and the subsequent collapse of several nations' self-sufficiency.

Although not without conflict, [[European ]]' early interactions with First Nations and Inuit populations were relatively peaceful. First Nations and Métis peoples played a critical part in the development of [[Former colonies and territories in |European colonies in ]], particularly for their role in assisting European [[coureur des bois|coureurs des bois]] and [[voyageurs]] in their explorations of the continent during the [[North  fur trade]]. These early European interactions with First Nations would change from [[Peace and Friendship Treaties|friendship and peace treaties]] to the [[Numbered Treaties|dispossession of Indigenous lands through treaties]]. From the late 18th century, European  forced Indigenous peoples to assimilate into a western  society. [[Settler colonialism in |Settler colonialism]] reached a climax in the late 19th and early 20th centuries. A period of redress began with the formation of a [[Truth and Reconciliation Commission of |reconciliation commission]] by the [[Government of ]] in 2008. This included acknowledgment of [[ genocide of Indigenous peoples|cultural genocide]], [[ Residential Schools Settlement Agreement|settlement agreements]], and betterment of racial discrimination issues, such as addressing the plight of [[missing and murdered Indigenous women]].

===European colonization===
[[File:Nouvelle- map-en.svg|upright=1.3|thumb|Map of territorial claims in [[North America]] by 1750. Possessions of [[ America]] (pink), [[New ]] (blue), and [[New ]] (orange); California, Pacific Northwest, and Great Basin not indicated.]]
It is believed that the first documented European to explore the east coast of  was [[Vikings|Norse]] explorer [[Leif Erikson]]. In approximately 1000 AD, the Norse built a small short-lived encampment that was occupied sporadically for perhaps 20 years at [[L'Anse aux Meadows]] on the northern tip of [[Newfoundland]]. No further European exploration occurred until 1497, when seafarer [[John Cabot]] explored and claimed 's [[Atlantic |Atlantic coast]] in the name of [[Henry VII of England]]. In 1534,  explorer Jacques Cartier explored the [[Gulf of  Lawrence]] where, on July 24, he planted a {{convert|10|m|ft|adj=on}} cross bearing the words, "long live the King of ", and took possession of the territory New  in the name of [[Francis I of |King Francis I]]. The early 16th century saw European mariners with navigational techniques pioneered by the [[Basques|Basque]] and [[ discoveries|]] establish seasonal whaling and fishing outposts along the Atlantic coast. In general, early settlements during the [[Age of Discovery]] appear to have been [[Population of #Ephemeral European settlements|short-lived]] due to a combination of the harsh climate, problems with navigating trade routes and competing outputs in Scandinavia.

In 1583, Sir [[Humphrey Gilbert]], by the [[royal prerogative]] of Queen [[Elizabeth I]], founded [[St. John's, Newfoundland and Labrador|St John's, Newfoundland]], as the first North  [[ overseas possessions| seasonal camp]]. In 1600, the  established their first seasonal trading post at [[Tadoussac]] along the  Lawrence.  explorer [[Samuel de Champlain]] arrived in 1603 and established the first permanent year-round European settlements at [[Port-Royal (Acadia)|Port Royal]] (in 1605) and Quebec City (in 1608). Among the [[ colonization of the Americas|colonists]] of New , ''[[ |Canadiens]]'' extensively settled the  Lawrence River valley and [[Acadians]] settled the present-day [[The Maritimes|Maritimes]], while fur traders and [[Catholic Church and the Age of Discovery|Catholic missionaries]] explored the [[Great Lakes]], [[Hudson Bay]], and the [[Mississippi watershed]] to [[Louisiana (New )|Louisiana]]. The [[Beaver Wars]] broke out in the mid-17th century over control of the North  fur trade.

The  established additional settlements in [[Newfoundland (island)|Newfoundland]] in 1610 along with settlements in the [[Thirteen Colonies]] to the south. A series of [[ and  Wars|four wars]] erupted in colonial North America between 1689 and 1763; the later wars of the period constituted the North  theatre of the [[Seven Years' War]]. Mainland [[Nova Scotia]] came under  rule with the 1713 [[Treaty of Utrecht]] and  and most of New  came under  rule in 1763 after the Seven Years' War.

=== North America===
[[File:Benjamin West 005.jpg|thumb|alt=Painting of General Wolfe dying in front of the  flag while attended by officers and native allies|[[Benjamin West]]'s ''[[The Death of General Wolfe]]'' (1771) dramatizes [[James Wolfe]]'s death during the [[Battle of the Plains of Abraham]] at [[Quebec City]].]]

The [[Royal Proclamation of 1763]] established First Nation treaty rights, created the [[Province of Quebec (1763–1791)|Province of Quebec]] out of New , and annexed [[Cape Breton Island]] to Nova Scotia. St John's Island (now [[Prince Edward Island]]) became a separate colony in 1769. To avert conflict in [[Quebec]], the  Parliament passed the [[Quebec Act]] 1774, expanding Quebec's territory to the Great Lakes and [[Ohio River|Ohio Valley]]. More importantly, the Quebec Act afforded Quebec special autonomy and rights of self-administration at a time when the Thirteen Colonies were increasingly agitating against  rule. It re-established the  language, Catholic faith, and [[Law of | civil law]] there, staving off the growth of an independence movement in contrast to the Thirteen Colonies. The Proclamation and the Quebec Act in turn angered many residents of the Thirteen Colonies, further fuelling anti- sentiment in the years prior to the [[ Revolution]].

After the successful  War of Independence, the [[Treaty of Paris (1783)|1783 Treaty of Paris]] recognized the independence of the newly formed [[]] and set the terms of peace, ceding [[ North America]]n territories south of the Great Lakes and east of the Mississippi River to the new country. The  war of independence also caused a large out-migration of [[Loyalists]], the settlers who had fought against  independence. Many moved to , particularly Atlantic , where their arrival changed the demographic distribution of the existing territories. [[New Brunswick]] was in turn split from Nova Scotia as part of a reorganization of Loyalist settlements in the Maritimes, which led to the incorporation of [[ John, New Brunswick]], as 's first city. To accommodate the influx of -speaking Loyalists in Central , the [[Constitutional Act 1791|Constitutional Act of 1791]] divided the province of  into -speaking Lower  (later [[Quebec]]) and -speaking Upper  (later [[Ontario# West (1841–1867)|Ontario]]), granting each its own elected legislative assembly.
[[File:Laura Secord warns Fitzgibbons, 1813.jpg|thumb|alt=Painting of Laura Secord warning  commander James FitzGibbon of an impending  attack at Beaver Dams|[[War of 1812]] heroine [[Laura Secord]] warning  commander [[James FitzGibbon]] of an [[Battle of Beaver Dams|impending  attack at Beaver Dams]]]]

The  were the main front in the [[War of 1812]] between the  and the [[ of Great Britain and |]]. Peace came in 1815; no boundaries were changed. Immigration resumed at a higher level, with over {{formatnum:960000}} arrivals from Britain between 1815 and 1850. New arrivals included refugees escaping the [[Great  Famine]] as well as [[ Gaelic|Gaelic]]-speaking Scots displaced by the [[Highland Clearances]]. Infectious diseases killed between 25 and 33 percent of Europeans who immigrated to  before 1891.

The desire for [[responsible government]] resulted in the abortive [[Rebellions of 1837]]. The [[Durham Report]] subsequently recommended responsible government and the assimilation of   into  culture. The [[Act of Union 1840]] merged the  into a united Province of  and responsible government was established for all provinces of  North America east of Lake Superior by 1855. The signing of the [[Oregon Treaty]] by Britain and the  in 1846 ended the [[Oregon boundary dispute]], extending the border westward along the [[49th parallel north|49th parallel]]. This paved the way for  colonies on [[Colony of Vancouver Island|Vancouver Island (1849)]] and in [[Colony of  Columbia (1858–1866)| Columbia (1858)]]. The Anglo- [[Treaty of  Petersburg (1825)]] established the border along the Pacific coast, but, even after the US [[Alaska Purchase]] of 1867, disputes continued about the exact demarcation of the Alaska–Yukon and Alaska– Columbia border.

===Confederation and expansion===
[[File: provinces evolution 2.gif|thumb|upright=1.3|alt=Refer to caption|Animated map showing [[Territorial evolution of |the growth and change of 's provinces and territories]] since Confederation in 1867]]

Following three constitutional conferences, the ''[[Constitution Act, 1867| North America Act, 1867]]'' officially proclaimed  Confederation on July 1, 1867, initially with four provinces: [[Ontario]], Quebec, Nova Scotia, and New Brunswick.  assumed control of [[Rupert's Land]] and the [[North-Western Territory]] to form the [[Northwest Territories]], where the Métis' grievances ignited the [[Red River Rebellion]] and the creation of the province of [[Manitoba]] in July 1870.  Columbia and Vancouver Island (which [[Colony of  Columbia (1866–1871)|had been united]] in 1866) joined the confederation in 1871 on the promise of a transcontinental railway extending to Victoria in the province within 10 years, while Prince Edward Island joined in 1873. In 1898, during the [[Klondike Gold Rush]] in the Northwest Territories, Parliament created the Yukon Territory. [[Alberta]] and [[Saskatchewan]] became provinces in 1905. Between 1871 and 1896, almost one quarter of the  population emigrated south to the US.

To open [[Western |the West]] and encourage European immigration, the Government of  sponsored the construction of three transcontinental railways (including the [[ Pacific Railway]]), passed the ''[[Dominion Lands Act]]'' to regulate settlement and established the [[North-West Mounted Police]] to assert authority over the territory. This [[Post-Confederation  (1867–1914)#Expansion|period of westward expansion]] and [[National Policy|nation building]] resulted in the displacement of many [[Plains |Indigenous peoples of the  Prairies]] to "[[ reserve]]s", clearing the way for ethnic European [[block settlement]]s. This caused the collapse of the [[History of bison conservation in #Plains bison|Plains Bison in western ]] and the introduction of European [[Agriculture in |cattle farms and wheat fields]] dominating the land. The Indigenous peoples saw widespread famine and disease due to the loss of the bison and their traditional hunting lands. The federal government did provide emergency relief, on condition of the Indigenous peoples moving to the reserves. During this time,  introduced the ''[[ Act]]'' extending its control over the First Nations to education, government and legal rights.

===Early 20th century===

Because Britain still maintained control of 's foreign affairs under the  North America Act, 1867, its declaration of war in 1914 automatically brought [[Military history of  during World War I| into the First World War]]. Volunteers sent to the [[Western Front (World War I)|Western Front]] later became part of the [[ Corps]], which played a substantial role in the [[Battle of Vimy Ridge]] and other major engagements of the war. The [[Conscription Crisis of 1917]] erupted when the [[Unionist Party ()|Unionist]] Cabinet's proposal to augment the military's dwindling number of active members with [[conscription]] was met with vehement objections from -speaking Quebecers. In 1919,  joined the [[League of Nations]] independently of Britain, and the ''[[Statute of Westminster, 1931]]'', affirmed 's independence.

The [[Great Depression in ]] during the early 1930s saw an economic downturn, leading to hardship across the country. In response to the downturn, the [[Co-operative Commonwealth Federation]] (CCF) in Saskatchewan introduced many elements of a [[welfare state]] (as pioneered by [[Tommy Douglas]]) in the 1940s and 1950s. On the advice of Prime Minister [[William Lyon Mackenzie King]], [[Declaration of war by #Nazi |war with  was declared]] effective September 10, 1939, by King [[George VI]], seven days after the . The delay underscored 's independence.

The first  Army units arrived in Britain in December 1939. In all, over a million  served in the armed forces during the [[Second World War]].  troops played important roles in many key battles of the war, including the failed 1942 [[Dieppe Raid]], the [[Allied invasion of ]], the [[Normandy landings]], the [[Operation Overlord|Battle of Normandy]], and the [[Battle of the Scheldt]] in 1944.  provided asylum for the [[ monarchy]] while that country was [[Reichskommissariat Niederlande|occupied]] and is credited by the  for major contributions to [[Liberation Day ()|its liberation]] from [[Nazi ]]. Despite another [[Conscription Crisis of 1944|conscription crisis in Quebec in 1944]],  finished the war with a large army and strong economy.

===Contemporary era===
The financial crisis of the Great Depression led the [[Dominion of Newfoundland]] to relinquish responsible government in 1934 and become a [[Crown colony]] ruled by a  governor. After two [[1948 Newfoundland referendums|referendums]], Newfoundlanders voted to join  in 1949 as a province.

's post-war economic growth, combined with the policies of successive Liberal governments, led to the emergence of a new [[ identity]], marked by the adoption of the [[Flag of |maple leaf flag]] in 1965, the implementation of [[official bilingualism]] ( and ) in 1969, and the institution of [[Multiculturalism#|official multiculturalism]] in 1971. [[Socially democratic]] programs were also instituted, such as [[Medicare ()|Medicare]], the [[ Pension Plan]], and [[Student financial aid in | Student Loans]]; though, provincial governments, particularly Quebec and Alberta, opposed many of these as incursions into their jurisdictions.
[[File: Charter of Rights and Freedoms ().jpg|thumb|A copy of the ''[[ Charter of Rights and Freedoms]]''|alt=refer to caption]]

Finally, another series of constitutional conferences resulted in the '' Act 1982'', the [[patriation]] of 's constitution from the , concurrent with the creation of the ''[[ Charter of Rights and Freedoms]]''.  had established complete sovereignty as an independent country under [[Monarchy of |its own monarchy]]. In 1999, [[Nunavut]] became 's third territory after a series of negotiations with the federal government.

At the same time, Quebec underwent profound social and economic changes through the [[Quiet Revolution]] of the 1960s, giving birth to a secular [[Quebec nationalism|nationalist]] movement. The radical [[Front de libération du Québec]] (FLQ) ignited the [[October Crisis]] with a series of bombings and kidnappings in 1970, and the [[Quebec sovereignty movement|{{Not a typo|sovereigntist}}]] [[Parti Québécois]] was elected in 1976, organizing an [[1980 Quebec referendum|unsuccessful referendum]] on sovereignty-association in 1980. Attempts to accommodate Quebec nationalism constitutionally through the [[Meech Lake Accord]] failed in 1990. This led to the formation of the [[Bloc Québécois]] in Quebec and the invigoration of the [[Reform Party of ]] in the West. A [[1995 Quebec referendum|second referendum]] followed in 1995, in which sovereignty was rejected by a slimmer margin of 50.6 to 49.4 percent. In 1997, the [[Supreme Court of |Supreme Court]] ruled [[Reference Re Secession of Quebec|unilateral secession]] by a province would be unconstitutional, and the [[Clarity Act]] was passed by Parliament, outlining the terms of a negotiated departure from Confederation.

In addition to the issues of Quebec sovereignty, a number of crises shook  society in the late 1980s and early 1990s. These included the explosion of [[Air  Flight 182]] in 1985, the largest mass murder in  history; the [[École Polytechnique massacre]] in 1989, a [[School shooting|university shooting]] targeting female students; and the [[Oka Crisis]] of 1990, the first of a number of violent confrontations between provincial governments and Indigenous groups.  joined the [[Gulf War]] in 1990 and was active in [[List of  peacekeeping missions|several peacekeeping missions]] in the 1990s, including operations in the [[Balkans]] during and after the [[Yugoslav Wars]], and in [[]], resulting in an incident that has been described as "[[ affair|the darkest era in the history of the  military]]".  sent [[ in the War in |troops to  in 2001]], resulting in the largest amount of [[ Forces casualties in | deaths]] for any single military mission since the [[ in the  War| War]] in the early 1950s.

In 2011,  forces participated in the [[NATO]]-led intervention into the [[First  Civil War| Civil War]] and also became involved in battling the [[Islamic State]] insurgency in  in the mid-2010s. The [[COVID-19 pandemic in ]] began on January 27, 2020, causing widespread social and economic disruption. In 2021, [[  residential school gravesites|possible gravesites of Indigenous children]] were found near former [[  residential school system| residential schools]], highlighting the [[ genocide of Indigenous peoples|cultural genocide against Indigenous peoples]]. A [[2025  trade war with  and |trade war involving the ]] began on February 1, 2025, when U.S. president [[Donald Trump]] signed [[Second Trump tariffs|orders imposing tariffs]] on goods entering the .
== History ==
{{Main|History of }}

{{For timeline|Timeline of  history}}

=== Prehistory ===
{{Main|Linear Pottery culture|Unetice culture|Urnfield culture|Celts}}

Ancient humans were present in  at least 600,000 years ago. The first non-modern human fossil (the [[Neanderthal]]) was discovered in the [[Neandertal (valley)|Neander Valley]]. Similarly dated evidence of modern humans has been found in the [[Caves and Ice Age Art in the Swabian Jura|Swabian Jura]], including 42,000-year-old [[Paleolithic flute|flutes]] which are the oldest musical instruments ever found, the 40,000-year-old [[Lion-man|Lion Man]], and the 41,000-year-old [[Venus of Hohle Fels]].

=== Germanic tribes, Roman frontier and the Frankish Empire ===
{{Main|Jastorf culture|Germanic peoples|Germania|Migration Period|Frankish Realm}}

[[File:Trier 012.JPG|thumb|[[Aula Palatina|Basilica of Constantine]] in [[Trier]] (''[[Augusta Treverorum]]''), built in the 4th century]]
The [[Germanic peoples]] are thought to have [[Ethnogenesis|emerged]] from the [[Jastorf culture]] during the [[Nordic Bronze Age]] or early [[Pre-Roman Iron Age|Iron Age]]. From southern [[Scandinavia]] and [[northern ]], they expanded south, east, and west, coming into contact with the [[Celts|Celtic]], [[ peoples|]], [[Balts|Baltic]], and [[Early Slavs|Slavic]] tribes. Southern  was inhabited by Celtic-speaking peoples, who belonged to the wider [[La Tène culture]]. They were later assimilated by the Germanic conquerors.

Under [[Augustus]], the [[Roman Empire]] began to invade lands inhabited by the Germanic tribes, creating a short-lived Roman province of [[Germania Antiqua|Germania]] between the Rhine and [[Elbe]] rivers. In 9 AD, three [[Roman legion]]s were [[Battle of the Teutoburg Forest|defeated]] by [[Arminius]] in the [[Battle of the Teutoburg Forest]]. The outcome of this battle dissuaded the Romans from their ambition of conquering [[Germania]] and is thus considered one of the most important events in [[European history]].{{sfn|Murdoch|2004|p=57}} By 100 AD, when [[Tacitus]] wrote ''[[Germania (book)|Germania]]'', Germanic tribes had settled along the Rhine and the Danube (the [[Limes Germanicus]]), occupying most of modern . However, [[Baden Württemberg|Baden-Württemberg]], southern [[Bavaria]], southern [[Hesse]] and the western [[Rhineland]] had [[Germanic Wars|been incorporated]] into [[Roman province]]s.{{sfn|Fulbrook |1991|pp=9–13}}

Around 260, Germanic peoples broke into Roman-controlled lands. After the invasion of the [[Huns]] in 375, and with the decline of Rome from 395, Germanic tribes moved farther southwest: the Franks established the [[Frankish Kingdom]] and pushed east to subjugate [[Duchy of Saxony|Saxony]] and [[Duchy of Bavaria|Bavaria]]. Areas of modern eastern  were inhabited by [[West Slavs|Western Slavic]] tribes.{{sfn|Fulbrook |1991|pp=9–13}}

{{Clear left}}

=== East Francia and the Holy Roman Empire ===
{{Main|East Francia|Holy Roman Empire}}

[[File:East Francia 843.svg|thumb|[[East Francia]] in 843]]
[[File:Lucas Cranach d.Ä. - Martin Luther, 1528 (Veste Coburg).jpg|thumb|upright|[[Martin Luther]], born in [[Eisleben]] in 1483, challenged the indulgences of the [[Catholic Church]], giving rise to the [[Reformation]] and [[Protestantism]].]]
[[Charlemagne]] founded the [[Carolingian Empire]] in 800; it was [[Treaty of Verdun|divided in 843]].{{sfn|Fulbrook |1991|p= 11}} The eastern successor kingdom of [[East Francia]] stretched from the Rhine in the west to the Elbe river in the east and from the North Sea to the Alps.{{sfn|Fulbrook |1991|p= 11}} Subsequently, the Holy Roman Empire emerged from it. The [[Ottonian]] rulers (919–1024) consolidated several major [[Stem duchy|duchies]]. In 996, [[Pope Gregory V|Gregory V]] became the first  Pope, appointed by his cousin [[Otto III]], whom he shortly after crowned Holy Roman Emperor. The Holy Roman Empire absorbed northern  and [[Burgundy (historical region)|Burgundy]] under the [[Salian]] emperors (1024–1125), although the emperors lost power through the [[Investiture Controversy]].

Under the [[House of Hohenstaufen|Hohenstaufen]] emperors (1138–1254),  princes encouraged  settlement to the south and east ({{lang|de|[[Ostsiedlung]]}}).{{sfn|Fulbrook |1991|pp= 19–20}} Members of the [[Hanseatic League]], mostly north  towns, prospered in the expansion of trade.{{sfn|Fulbrook |1991|pp= 13–24}} The population declined starting with the [[Great Famine of 1315–1317|Great Famine]] in 1315, followed by the [[Black Death]] of 1348–1350. The [[Golden Bull of 1356|Golden Bull]] issued in 1356 provided the constitutional structure of the Empire and codified the election of the emperor by seven [[prince-elector]]s.{{sfn|Fulbrook |1991|p= 27}}

[[Johannes Gutenberg]] introduced moveable-type printing to Europe, laying the basis for the [[democratization of knowledge|democratisation of knowledge]]. In 1517, [[Martin Luther]] incited the Protestant Reformation and [[Luther Bible|his translation of the Bible]] began the standardisation of the language; the 1555 [[Peace of Augsburg]] tolerated the "Evangelical" faith ([[Lutheranism]]), but also decreed that the faith of the prince was to be the faith of his subjects ({{lang|la|[[cuius regio, eius religio]]}}). From the [[Cologne War]] through the [[Thirty Years' War]]s (1618–1648), religious conflict devastated  lands and significantly reduced the population.

The [[Peace of Westphalia]] ended religious warfare among the [[Imperial Estate]]s. The legal system initiated by a series of [[Imperial Reform]]s (approximately 1495–1555) provided for considerable local autonomy and a stronger [[Imperial Diet (Holy Roman Empire)|Imperial Diet]]. The [[House of Habsburg]] held the imperial crown from 1438 until the death of [[Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor|Charles VI]] in 1740. Following the [[War of the  Succession]] and the [[Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (1748)|Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle]], Charles VI's daughter [[Maria Theresa]] ruled as [[Queen consort|empress consort]] when her husband, [[Francis I, Holy Roman Emperor|Francis I]], became emperor.

From 1740, [[ dualism|dualism]] between the  [[Habsburg monarchy]] and the [[Kingdom of Prussia]] dominated  history. In 1772, 1793, and 1795, Prussia and , along with the [[ Empire]], agreed to the [[Partitions of ]]. During the period of the [[ Revolutionary Wars]], the [[Napoleonic era]] and the subsequent [[Final Recess of the Reichsdeputation|final meeting of the Imperial Diet]], most of the [[Free Imperial Cities]] were annexed by dynastic territories; the ecclesiastical territories were secularised and annexed. In 1806 the {{lang|de|Imperium}} was dissolved; , , Prussia, and the Habsburgs () competed for hegemony in the  states during the [[Napoleonic Wars]].{{sfn|Fulbrook |1991|p= 97}}

===  Confederation and Empire ===
{{Main| question| Confederation|Unification of | Empire| colonial empire}}

[[File: Confederation (1815).svg|thumb|The  Confederation in 1815]]
Following the fall of [[Napoleon]], the [[Congress of Vienna]] founded the  Confederation, a loose league of [[States of the  Confederation|39 sovereign states]]. The appointment of the [[emperor of ]] as the permanent president reflected the Congress's rejection of [[Prussia]]'s rising influence. Disagreement within [[Concert of Europe|restoration]] politics partly led to the rise of [[Liberalism in |liberal]] movements, followed by new measures of repression by  statesman [[Klemens von Metternich]]. The {{lang|de|[[Zollverein]]}}, a tariff union, furthered economic unity. In light of [[Revolutions of 1848|revolutionary movements in Europe]], intellectuals and commoners started the [[ revolutions of 1848–1849|revolutions of 1848 in the  states]], raising the  question. King [[Frederick William IV of Prussia]] was offered the title of emperor, but with a loss of power; he rejected the crown and the proposed constitution, a temporary setback for the movement.

[[File:Berlin Nationaldenkmal Kaiser Wilhelm mit Schloss 1900.jpg|thumb|right|[[Berlin Palace]], the main residence of the Kings of Prussia and  Emperors]]
King [[William I,  Emperor|William I]] appointed [[Otto von Bismarck]] as the [[Minister President of Prussia]] in 1862. Bismarck successfully concluded the [[Second Schleswig War|war with  in 1864]]; the subsequent decisive Prussian victory in the [[Austro-Prussian War]] of 1866 enabled him to create the [[North  Confederation]] which excluded [[ Empire|]]. After the defeat of  in the [[Franco-Prussian War]], the  princes proclaimed the founding of the  Empire in 1871. Prussia was the dominant constituent state of the new empire; the King of Prussia ruled as its [[ Emperor|Emperor]] ({{lang|de|Kaiser}}), and Berlin became its capital.

In the {{lang|de|[[Gründerzeit]]}} period following the unification of , Bismarck's foreign policy as [[chancellor of ]] secured 's position as a great nation by forging alliances and avoiding war. However, under [[Wilhelm II]],  took an [[New Imperialism|imperialistic]] course, leading to friction with neighbouring countries. [[Dual Alliance (1879)|A dual alliance]] was created with the [[multinational state|multinational realm]] of [[-]]; the [[Triple Alliance (1882)|Triple Alliance of 1882]] included . Britain,  and  also concluded alliances to protect against Habsburg interference with  interests in the Balkans or  interference against .{{sfn|Fulbrook |1991|pp= 135, 149}} At the [[Berlin Conference]] in 1884,  claimed several [[List of former  colonies|colonies]] including [[ East Africa]], [[ South West Africa]], [[Togoland]], and [[Kamerun]]. Later,  further expanded its colonial empire to include holdings in the Pacific and [[]]. The colonial government in South West Africa (present-day [[]]), from 1904 to 1908, carried out the [[Herero and Nama genocide|annihilation of the local Herero and Nama peoples]] as punishment for an uprising; this was the 20th century's first [[genocide]].

[[Assassination of Archduke Franz Ferdinand of |The assassination]] of [[Archduke Franz Ferdinand of |'s crown prince]] on 28 June 1914 provided the pretext for - to attack  and trigger [[World War I]]. After four years of warfare, in which approximately two million  soldiers were killed, [[Armistice with |a general armistice]] ended the fighting. In the [[ Revolution of 1918–1919| Revolution]] (November 1918), Wilhelm II and the ruling princes [[abdication|abdicated]] their positions, and  was declared a [[federal republic]]. 's new leadership signed the [[Treaty of Versailles]] in 1919, accepting defeat by the [[Allies of World War I|Allies]].  perceived the treaty as humiliating, which was seen by historians as influential in the rise of [[Adolf Hitler]].  lost around 13% of its European territory and ceded all of its colonial possessions.

=== Weimar Republic and Nazi  ===
{{Main|Weimar Republic|Nazi }}

[[File:Hitler portrait crop.jpg|thumb|[[Adolf Hitler]], dictatorial ''[[Führer]]'' of Nazi  from 1933 until [[Death of Adolf Hitler|his suicide]] in 1945|upright]]

<!-- deleted, see Talk page [[File:Europe under Nazi domination.png|thumb|A map of [[-occupied Europe]] in 1942 during [[World War II]] with areas controlled by the  Reich shown in bold black]] -->
On 11 August 1919, President [[Friedrich Ebert]] signed the democratic [[Weimar Constitution]].{{sfn|Fulbrook |1991|pp=156–160}} [[Bavarian Soviet Republic|Communists briefly seized power in Bavaria]] and a few larger cities, while conservative elements failed to overthrow the central government in the 1920 [[Kapp Putsch]]. The [[occupation of the Ruhr]] by  and  troops and a period of [[Hyperinflation in the Weimar Republic|hyperinflation]] followed. A [[Dawes Plan|plan to restructure 's war reparations]] and the creation of [[ Rentenmark|a new currency]] in 1924 helped stabilise the government and ushered in the [[Golden Twenties]], an era of artistic innovation and liberal cultural life.

The worldwide [[Great Depression]] hit  in 1929, and by 1932 the unemployment rate had risen to 24%. The [[Nazi Party]] led by Adolf Hitler became the largest party in the Reichstag after the [[July 1932  federal election|election of July 1932]], and [[President Hindenburg]] appointed Hitler chancellor on 30 January 1933.{{sfn|Fulbrook |1991|pp=155–158, 172–177}} After the [[Reichstag fire]], [[Reichstag Fire Decree|a decree]] abrogated basic [[civil rights]], and the first [[Nazi concentration camps|Nazi concentration camp]] opened. On 23 March 1933, the [[Enabling Act of 1933|Enabling Act]] gave Hitler unrestricted legislative power, overriding the constitution, and marked the beginning of Nazi . His government established a centralised [[Totalitarianism|totalitarian state]], [[1933  referendum|withdrew from the League of Nations]], and dramatically increased the [[ re-armament|country's rearmament]]. A government-sponsored programme for economic renewal focused on public works, the most famous of which was the {{lang|de|[[Reichsautobahn|Autobahn]]}}.

In 1935, the regime withdrew from the Treaty of Versailles and introduced the [[Nuremberg Laws]] which targeted [[Jews]] and other [[Minority group|minorities]].  also reacquired control of the [[Territory of the Saar Basin|Saarland]] in 1935,{{sfn|Fulbrook |1991|pp=188–189}} [[remilitarization of the Rhineland|remilitarised the Rhineland]] in 1936, [[Anschluss|annexed]]  in 1938, [[Sudetenland#Sudetenland as part of Nazi |annexed]] the Sudetenland in 1938 with the [[Munich Agreement]], and, in violation of the agreement, [[ occupation of |occupied ]] in March 1939. {{lang|de|[[Kristallnacht]]}} (Night of Broken Glass) saw the burning of synagogues, the destruction of Jewish businesses, and mass arrests of Jewish people.

In August 1939, [[Government of Nazi |Hitler's government]] negotiated the [[Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact]] that divided Eastern Europe into  and [[Soviet Union|Soviet]] spheres of influence. On 1 September 1939,  [[invasion of |invaded ]], beginning [[European theatre of World War II|World War II in Europe]];{{sfn|Fulbrook |1991|pp=190–195}} Britain and  declared war on  on 3 September. In the spring of 1940,  [[Operation Weserübung|conquered  and ]], [[ invasion of the |the ]], [[ invasion of  (1940)|]], [[ invasion of |]], and [[Battle of |]], forcing the  government to sign an [[armistice]]. The  repelled  air attacks in the [[Battle of Britain]] in the same year. In 1941,  troops [[Invasion of Yugoslavia|invaded Yugoslavia]], [[Battle of |]] and the [[Operation Barbarossa|Soviet Union]], and  declared war on the . By 1942,  and its allies controlled most of [[-occupied Europe|continental Europe]] and [[North Africa]], but following the Soviet victory at the [[Battle of Stalingrad]], the Allied [[North African Campaign|reconquest of North Africa]] and [[ Campaign (World War II)|invasion of ]] in 1943,  forces suffered repeated military defeats. In 1944, the Soviets [[Eastern Front (World War II)#Summer 1944|pushed into Eastern Europe]]; the Western allies [[Operation Overlord|landed in ]] and entered  despite a [[Battle of the Bulge|final  counteroffensive]]. Following [[Death of Adolf Hitler|Hitler's suicide]] during the [[Battle of Berlin]], [[ Instrument of Surrender| signed the surrender document]] on 8 May 1945, [[End of World War II in Europe|ending World War II in Europe]]{{sfn|Fulbrook |1991|pp=190–195}} and Nazi . Following the end of the war, surviving Nazi officials were tried for [[War crimes of the Wehrmacht|war crimes]] at the [[Nuremberg trials]].

In what later became known as [[the Holocaust]], the  government persecuted [[Holocaust victims|minorities]], including interning them in concentration and [[Extermination camp|death camps]] across Europe. The regime systematically murdered around 6 million [[Jews]], at least 130,000 [[Porajmos|Romani]], 275,000 [[Aktion T4|disabled]], thousands of [[Jehovah's Witnesses]], thousands of [[Persecution of homosexuals in Nazi |homosexuals]], and hundreds of thousands of [[Nacht und Nebel|political and religious opponents]]. [[Generalplan Ost|Nazi policies in -occupied countries]] resulted in the deaths of an estimated 2.7&nbsp;million [[ people|Poles]], 1.3&nbsp;million [[]], 1&nbsp;million [[]] and 3.5&nbsp;million [[ mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war|Soviet prisoners of war]]. [[ casualties in World War II| military casualties]] have been estimated at 5.3&nbsp;million, and around 900,000  civilians died. Around 12&nbsp;million [[Flight and expulsion of  (1944–1950)|ethnic  were expelled]] from across Eastern Europe, and  lost roughly [[Former eastern territories of |one-quarter]] of its pre-war territory.

=== East and West  ===
{{Main|History of  (1945–1990)|Allied-occupied |West |East }}

[[File:Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG|thumb|The [[fall of the Berlin Wall]] in 1989 was one of the first developments in the end of the [[Cold War]], leading ultimately to the dissolution of the [[Soviet Union]].]]

After the surrender of Nazi , the [[Allies of World War II|Allies]] ''[[de jure]]'' [[Berlin Declaration (1945)|abolished the  state]] and partitioned Berlin and 's remaining territory into four occupation zones. The western sectors, controlled by , the [[]], and the [[]], were merged on 23 May 1949 to form the Federal Republic of  (FRG) ({{langx|de|Bundesrepublik Deutschland}}); on 7 October 1949, the Soviet Zone became the  Democratic Republic (GDR) ({{lang|de|Deutsche Demokratische Republik}}; DDR). They were informally known as West  and East . East  selected [[East Berlin]] as its capital, while West  chose [[Bonn]] as a provisional capital to emphasise its stance that the two-state solution was temporary.

West  was established as a federal parliamentary republic with a [[social market economy]]. In 1948, West  became a major recipient of reconstruction aid under the  [[Marshall Plan]]. [[Konrad Adenauer]] was elected the first [[Federal Chancellor of the Federal Republic of |federal chancellor of ]] in 1949. The country enjoyed prolonged economic growth ({{lang|de|[[Wirtschaftswunder]]}}) beginning in the early 1950s. West  joined [[NATO]] in 1955 and was a founding member of the [[European Economic Community]]. On 1 January 1957, the [[Saar Protectorate|Saarland]] joined West .

East  was an [[Eastern Bloc]] state under political and military control by the [[Soviet Union]] via occupation forces and the [[Warsaw Pact]]. Although East  claimed to be a democracy, political power was exercised solely by leading members ({{lang|de|[[Politburo|Politbüro]]}}) of the communist-controlled [[Socialist Unity Party of ]], supported by the {{lang|de|[[Stasi]]|italic=no}}, an immense secret service. While [[Communist propaganda|East  propaganda]] was based on the benefits of the GDR's social programmes and the alleged threat of a West  invasion, many of its citizens looked to the West for freedom and prosperity. The [[Berlin Wall]], built in 1961, prevented East  citizens from escaping to West , becoming a symbol of the [[Cold War]].

Tensions between East and West  were reduced in the late 1960s by Chancellor [[Willy Brandt]]'s {{lang|de|[[Ostpolitik]]}}. In 1989,  decided to dismantle the [[Iron Curtain]] and [[Removal of 's border fence with |open its border with ]], causing the emigration of thousands of East  to West  via  and . This had devastating effects on the GDR, where [[Monday demonstrations in East |regular mass demonstrations]] received increasing support. In an effort to help retain East  as a state, the East  authorities eased border restrictions, but this actually led to an acceleration of the {{lang|de|Wende}} reform process, culminating in the ''[[Treaty on the Final Settlement with Respect to |Two Plus Four Treaty]]'' under which  regained full sovereignty. This permitted [[ reunification]] on 3 October 1990, with the accession of the [[New states of |five re-established states]] of the former GDR. The [[fall of the Berlin Wall]] in 1989 became a symbol of the [[fall of Communism]], the [[dissolution of the Soviet Union]],  reunification and {{lang|de|[[Die Wende]]}} ("the turning point").

=== Reunified  and the European Union ===
{{Main| reunification|History of  since 1990}}

[[File:Berlin reichstag west panorama 2.jpg|thumb|right|The [[Berlin/Bonn Act]] made [[Berlin]] the [[capital of ]] again, with the [[Reichstag building|Reichstag]] becoming the seat of the [[ parliament]] in 1999.]]
United  was considered the enlarged continuation of [[West ]], so it retained its memberships in international organisations. Based on the [[Berlin/Bonn Act]] (1994), [[Berlin]] again became the [[capital of ]], while [[Bonn]] obtained the unique status of a {{lang|de|Bundesstadt}} (federal city), retaining some federal ministries. The relocation of the government was completed in 1999, and modernisation of the East  economy was scheduled to last until 2019.

Since reunification,  has taken a more active role in the [[European Union]], signing the [[Maastricht Treaty]] in 1992 and the [[Lisbon Treaty]] in 2007, and co-founding the [[eurozone]].  sent a peacekeeping force to secure stability in the [[1999 NATO bombing in Yugoslavia|Balkans]] and sent [[Bundeswehr| troops]] to [[]] as part of a NATO effort to provide [[War in  (2001–2021)|security in that country]] after the ousting of the [[Taliban]].

In the [[2005  federal election|2005 elections]], [[Angela Merkel]] became the first female chancellor. In 2009, the  government approved a €50&nbsp;billion stimulus plan. Among the major  political projects of the early 21st century are the advancement of [[European integration]], the [[Energy transition in |country's energy transition]] ({{lang|de|Energiewende}}) for a [[sustainable energy]] supply, the [[Debt brake ()|debt brake]] for balanced budgets, measures to increase the [[Ageing of Europe#|fertility rate]] ([[Natalistic politics|pronatalism]]), and [[high-tech]] strategies for the transition of the  economy, summarised as [[Industry 4.0]]. During the [[2015 European migrant crisis]], the country took in over a million refugees and migrants.
==History==
{{Main|History of }}

===Prehistory===
{{See also|Megalithic Temples of |Ħal Saflieni Hypogeum|Għar Dalam}}

 has been inhabited from at least {{Circa|6500 BC}}, with the arrival of [[Mesolithic]] hunter-gatherers likely originating from Sicily. Discoveries at [[Latnija Cave]] led by the  archaeologist Eleanor Scerri included the remains of hearths, stone tools and an abundant and diverse range of animal bones. These included indigenous red deer that are now extinct, fish and marine mammals, as well as abundant edible marine [[gastropods]]. To arrive on , these hunter-gatherers had to cross around 100&nbsp;km of open water, documenting the longest yet-known sea crossing by hunter-gatherers in the Mediterranean. The extinction of the [[Hippopotamus melitensis|dwarf hippos]], [[Cygnus falconeri|giant swans]] and [[Palaeoloxodon falconeri|dwarf elephants]] has historically been linked to the earliest arrival of humans on . However this seems unlikely since recent work suggests these animals went extinct many thousands of years before the arrival of the first people, and no such animals were found in association with the earliest known Mesolithic hunter-gatherers. The claim for an earlier occupation of the island by [[Neanderthal]]s is widely rejected. <sup>Supplementary Information</sup> [[Early European Farmers|Neolithic Farmers]], also originating from Sicily, are thought to have arrived on the islands by around 5400 BC. Prehistoric farming settlements dating to the [[Early Neolithic]] include the [[Għar Dalam]] cave site in the uppermost layers associated with domesticated animals. The Neolithic population on  grew [[cereals]], raised livestock and, in common with other ancient Mediterranean cultures, worshipped a [[mother goddess|fertility figure]].

[[File:Ggantija Temples, Xaghra, Gozo.jpg|thumb|[[Ġgantija]] [[megalith]]ic temple complex]]
A culture of [[megalith]]ic temple builders then either supplanted or arose from this early period. Around 3500 BC, these people built some of the oldest existing free-standing structures in the world in the form of the megalithic [[Ġgantija]] temples on [[Gozo]]; other early temples include those at [[Ħaġar Qim]] and [[Mnajdra]]. The temples have distinctive architecture, typically a complex [[trefoil]] design, and were used from 4000 to 2500 BC. Tentative information suggests that [[animal sacrifice]]s were made to the goddess of fertility, whose statue is now in the National Museum of Archaeology in Valletta.
